<en> The next item is the report by Tom√°≈° Zatloukal , on behalf of the Committee on Culture and Education , on efficiency and equity in European education and training systems .
<sp>
<en> rapporteur . - ( CS ) Mr President , Commissioner , ladies and gentlemen , the European Union is facing a number of connected socioeconomic challenges : the emergence of highly competitive countries , the ageing of the population , migration , a fast-changing labour market structure , and booming information and communication technologies .
<en> Each one of these factors affects the issue of access to quality education .
<en> People with low qualifications are increasingly at risk of unemployment and social exclusion .
<en> Fair systems guarantee that education and training are independent of socioeconomic background and other factors that place individuals at a disadvantage .
<en> The challenge is to support the participation of pupils , students and adults from all social groups : the current situation in this regard is particularly unsatisfactory .
<en> The report I am tabling here in this Parliament urges Member States to take positive measures from the pre-school stage to ensure the social diversity of classes and establishments and run quality educational programmes .
<en> Skills that are hereditary or acquired at an early age provide the basis for learning in later life .
<en> The return on investment is highest during this period because the fruit of such investment lasts a lifetime .
<en> I would like to point out that at the level of primary education premature categorisation of pupils has a detrimental effect .
<en> Instead , I consider it important to adapt the curriculum so that it suits diverse groups of children and their capabilities within one school .
<en> On the other hand , differentiation and creating a flexible range of study options is very effective at secondary level .
<en> As far as vocational training is concerned , I would recommend improving access to tertiary education and developing opportunities for lifelong learning .
<en> Third-level education is vital to the success of a knowledge-based economy .
<en> It would benefit from more funding than it receives at present .
<en> The report states that free university tuition does not necessarily guarantee equity and calls for an analysis of the range of financial incentives and support options that can significantly reduce inequity in terms of access to university education .
<en> Education has an impact on the economy : it increases human capital and innovative capability and enables technology to be disseminated .
<en> Each additional year of average school attendance raises productivity in an average EU country selectively by 6.2 % and in the long term by a further 3.1 % , thanks to its contribution to more rapid technological development .
<en> Increasing the efficiency of education and training brings both individuals and society as a whole a return on investment of up to 8 % a year .
<en> A further benefit is a reduction in unemployment : in today 's EU the average unemployment rate is 12.6 % amongst people who have completed primary or secondary education , as against 5 % in the case of people who have completed higher education .
<en> Furthermore , recent research carried out by the Commission has shown that 75 million EU citizens - i.e. 32 % of the workforce - have received insufficient education .
<en> In 2010 only 15 % of new jobs will be available for that group of people , most of whom come from socially disadvantaged sectors of society .
<en> Education and training policies must have a significant positive impact on social and economic results , sustainable development and social cohesion , whereas inefficiency and inequity entail huge costs : loss of tax revenue , unemployment , a greater requirement for healthcare and support from public funds , and also the costs associated with a higher level of anti-social behaviour .
<en> Education and training are basic factors contributing to long-term European economic growth , to competitiveness and to social cohesion .
<en> In conclusion , allow me to thank all my colleagues who have worked with me on this report .
<sp>
<en> Member of the Commission . - Madam President , I really welcome this initiative of the Parliament to take further the message of our communication , which we adopted on this topic last year .
<en> I read your report with a lot of interest and I also listened now to Mr Zatloukal , whom I want to congratulate cordially because I think and I feel we are partners on this issue , in this debate and in efforts to improve the situation .
<en> We could listen now to a description of socioeconomic challenges that we are facing individually , collectively , together , but also of the importance of investment - better investment , more investment - in education and training policies .
<en> I think that education and training policy lies at the centre of our efforts to create a more prosperous and a more cohesive European society .
<en> All European education systems are marked by educational inequities that reflect socioeconomic inequalities .
<en> The paradoxical role of education and training in relation to these inequalities is that they very often contribute to their perpetuation .
<en> But they are sometimes the only vehicle by which inequalities can be ameliorated .
<en> Across Europe , the process of modernising education and training systems is largely driven by the search for greater efficiency in terms of cost-effectiveness .
<en> I think this is really desirable , of course , but it is frequently , and wrongly , assumed that efficiency and equity are mutually exclusive .
<en> As part of our commitment to helping Member States improve their education and training systems , the Commission 's communication showed that efficiency and equity do not have to come at the expense of each other , at the expense of quality .
<en> Efficiency and equity are , in effect , mutually enforcing .
<en> I think this is the most important message from the whole communication .
<en> Your report stresses strongly the need for European education and training systems to be both efficient and equitable if they are to help us to achieve not only economic growth but social cohesion .
<en> I am especially pleased to see your emphasis on the need to develop efficient and equitable policies for the whole life-long learning continuum and on the need to invest in education early , as investing in quality early-childhood and pre-primary education and care is shown to be the most effective way of breaking the cycle of disadvantage .
<en> I am also pleased to notice that you confirm our message that early tracking of pupils has detrimental effects on efficiency and equity .
<en> And , of course , you place a lot of emphasis on the need to develop a culture of evaluation in order to develop effective long-term policies and create policies based on solid evidence .
<en> Your initiative will bring us closer to the development of life-long learning strategies that foster equality , inclusion , integration , and social cohesion .
<en> We will take full account of it in our forthcoming initiatives in the field of education and training , especially in the proposal for the 2008 Joint Report on the implementation of our work programme and our reflections for the future , and in the Green Paper on the links between education and migration , in which inequalities will be a central issue .
<en> We hope to present this communication next spring .
<sp>
<en> draftsman of the opinion of the Committee on Women 's Rights and Gender Equality . - ( DE ) Madam President , the question is : why are we talking about equality or inequality when more women than men reach a high level of education ?
<en> What this means is that we have the same educational opportunities and we are utilising them as well , but equality of opportunity is no longer guaranteed after that .
<en> In training , in the use of their acquired knowledge , women continue to suffer discrimination , which means that there is still no equality in the education and training systems .
<en> That is why it is essential that we take account of women who are already mothers and are studying , for example , that we demand particularly flexible organisation of studies here , and that we promote and support access for young women , especially from remote regions , and vulnerable groups such as migrant women and women from ethnic minorities , for there are major anomalies and inequalities here .
<en> This must start at pre-school and school age and then continue all the way through to vocational training .

<en> on behalf of the PPE-DE Group . - ( HU ) Thank you , Madam President .
<en> I will speak in Hungarian .
<en> Commissioner , last week , representing the Committee on Culture and Education , I took part in a conference in Lisbon entitled ' Young Voices - Meeting Diversity in Education ' , organised by the Portuguese Presidency .
<en> It was a profoundly moving experience to hear young people living with a variety of physical and learning disabilities present their school experiences .
<en> There was one common feature in their story : every one of them said that they felt that if they were able to participate in school activities alongside their able-bodied peers , they would not be judged according to their disabilities but according to their abilities and personalities .
<en> Integrating children living with a disability into mainstream education alongside their able-bodied peers is also vital in order to ensure that society accepts them and includes them more easily as adults .
<en> If children are accustomed from an early age to being around children who have some disability or other , and are accustomed to having to respect them equally and perhaps to helping them , then there is a good chance that they will demonstrate more understanding and more empathy towards disadvantaged people in their adult lives .
<en> The report we have before us speaks a great deal about integration issues relating to social differences .
<en> I am convinced that , by analogy to the example I referred to above , it is also important for children who are socially disadvantaged to be able to participate in an inclusive way alongside other children in all the various stages of education .
<en> To achieve this , two things have to be put in place .
<en> One is technological progress and removal of barriers .
<en> From this point of view , central and eastern European Member States are lagging far behind : schools , the school environment , transport facilities , even the hospitals , other institutions , public institutions , for example , are all inaccessible to wheelchair users .
<en> The other , and this will take longer , is the change in attitude that is needed on the part of decision-makers in order for them to acknowledge that inclusive education is the first crucial stage in the process that leads to social acceptance and integration .
<en> In conclusion , let me say that sports , too , are an important tool for education and social leverage , because social and societal differences disappear in sports ; the only things that matter are talent , determination and application .
<en> Physical education in schools and sports contribute greatly to strengthening important social values such as solidarity and respect for each other 's dignity .
<en> This is why I consider it important that when this House debates the quality , efficiency and equity of education and training , reference should also be made to the importance of physical education and its quality , efficiency and equity .
<en> We also need to ensure that inclusive education in this regard plays a major part .
<en> I congratulate the rapporteur and thank you for your attention .

<en> ( SK ) Italian authorities have informed the Member States of the European Union , through the European Early Warning and Response System , about an outbreak of tropical fever spread by the chikungunya virus in the Emilia-Romagna region .
<en> They have reported 197 cases of the tropical virus .
<en> Laboratory tests have confirmed that 14 % of the total number of ill people have contracted the virus and it has claimed one victim .
<en> Although there is no reason to panic yet , the European Commission must once more take steps to prepare for the possibility of a large epidemic .
<en> The European Centre for Disease Prevention and Control , monitoring communicable diseases , notes that favourable climatic conditions allow the virus to spread , in particular in the Mediterranean region .
<en> The risk of the virus being transmitted to other European countries is also high .
<en> Infected people can initiate new transmission cycles in other regions of the Union .

<en> ( RO ) Statistics show that the European Union population is aging .
<en> Only 35 % of the European Union citizens are over 50 years old and only 16 % of the European Union population is under 14 years old .
<en> The European Union 's demographic policy is a policy that Europe 's future depends on .
<en> The demographic policy should refer to accessible health services and decent pensions for pensioners , measures to increase the birth-rate in all Member States , as well as to decent , stable and well paid jobs .
<en> For this reason , I ask the European Commission to develop , together with the Member States , a Community policy and national strategies as regards the demographic policy .
<en> The result of such measures will be seen in the next 20-30 years .
<en> Social Europe needs all its citizens and , especially , it needs each citizen to be integrated into society and have a decent living .
<en> This is why we have to correlate the population protection and development policies with the demographic policies .

<en> Member of the Commission . - The Commission appreciates the interest shown by Parliament in a review of the trade defence instruments ( TDIs ) and reiterates the importance it attaches to the views of Parliament in the context of the current review .
<en> It looks forward to the report by the Committee on International Trade , which it hopes will be completed soon .
<en> On its side , the Commission is finalising its response to the consultation process .
<en> Indeed , the Commission held a preliminary discussion , an orientation debate , before its meeting today on this subject .
<en> Proposals to the Council could be made in the next weeks .
<en> The Commission intends to keep Parliament closely involved and informed on this .
<en> The Commission has , of course , carefully examined all reactions to the Green Paper , of which there are many hundreds .
<en> The intention now is to inform Member States and Parliament of the main reactions and suggestions received , and these will also be published .
<en> They will be discussed by the Commission again before proposals are tabled to the Council , hopefully in the last half of November .
<en> Most stakeholders consulted and submitting their views share the Commission 's opinion that TDIs remain essential in a globalising world economy where multilaterally-agreed competition rules are lacking .
<en> Also , the majority of stakeholders do not see the need for a major overhaul of the TDI system .
<en> Neither does the Commission .
<en> However , there is also a wish for the rules to be made clearer , as well as for increased transparency and for there to be more efficient application of the instruments .
<en> The claim that the Commission has changed its approach towards the assessment of Community interest in some recent cases is simply not true .
<en> Each case has been examined on the basis of its own technical merits .
<en> Some cases have raised atypical issues , but they have been resolved in line with Community legislation and within the small discretion allowed by that legislation , after thorough discussion with Member States .
<en> Lastly , it is correct that no new anti-dumping investigations were initiated in the first half of 2007 .
<en> However , it should be pointed out that anti-dumping investigations are industry-driven and are not initiated by us .
<en> In other words , they are initiated on the basis of complaints from Community industry .
<en> In the first six months of 2007 , no complaints meeting the requirements of the law were lodged .
<en> It is not unusual that the number of initiations varies from one year to another , depending on factors such as the business cycle , over-capacity in third countries and diversion of trade as a result of trade defence measures in other world markets .
<en> The number of initiations has also fluctuated in past years .
<en> In 2003 , for example , the Commission initiated in total only eight new investigations , the first of which was initiated at the end of May in that year .
<en> Also , the first semester of 2007 followed a period of exceptionally high activity at the end of 2006 .
<en> Finally , I would draw your attention to the fact that in September 2007 two new anti-dumping investigations were initiated against imports from China : one for citric acid and another for monosodium glutamate .
<sp>

<en> Member of the Commission . - I am not quite sure what the honourable Member means by the ' liberalisation of our trade policy ' .
<en> By definition , trade can only take place when markets are opened and trade flows are , in effect , being liberalised .
<en> Trade does not take place behind closed borders or where economies are being converted into fortresses , so of course the Commission seeks to promote the liberalisation of trade .
<en> The Global Europe trade policy review and strategy that was presented and agreed by the Commission and the Member States a year ago sets out very clearly the interests of the European Union , which are to maintain open markets at home , to promote and use multilateral and bilateral negotiations , to open markets abroad and to use effective trade defence measures to tackle unfair trade or unfair competition .
<en> Those are the three legs of our strategy ; each is equally important .
<en> The review of the third leg of that tripod is taking place after quite dramatic changes have taken place in the world economy , and indeed in the European economy , since the last review of our trade defence measures took place , which was over 10 years ago .
<en> We have a responsibility to make sure that our measures are operating as well as they could be and that they command consensus and support and solidarity amongst our Member States .
<en> When that weakens , the trade defence measures become less easy or possible to use .
<en> It is in an effort to rebuild and restore that consensus , support and solidarity amongst our Member States that we are undertaking this review .

<en> in writing . - ( HU ) Smoking is a major public health problem that claims several hundred thousand victims every year , including non-smokers .
<en> As this is a problem on a global scale , it calls for multifaceted action , commitment on the part of Member States , and effective legislation that is even tougher than hitherto .
<en> Protection of European citizens ' health demands this .
<en> Clearly , the road to achieving the primary objective , a smoke-free Europe , will be a long one , requiring tremendous effort and commitment .
<en> For this reason , we have to take things one step at a time .
<en> Several Member States have set an example that we should follow , taking sound and effective action to avert the dangers of passive smoking .
<en> One of the next steps should be to introduce a complete ban on smoking in all enclosed workplaces , including the catering sector , all public buildings and all public transport within two years throughout the whole of the European Union .
<en> To combat smoking successfully , we need a sound basis , a comprehensive Community strategy based on relevant studies and the best empirical knowledge , aimed at controlling smoking and encouraging people to quit .
<en> Planning effective legislative measures , prevention and education all have a key role to play in such a strategy .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( ET ) Ladies and gentlemen , every year cigarette smoking leads over 650 000 Europeans to a premature death .
<en> None of them decides to take up smoking in the desire to kill themselves .
<en> Smokers are addicts , slaves of persistent , decades-long propaganda .
<en> Only tough PR can explain the fact that whilst 86 % of Europeans believe that the workplace should be smoke-free , only 61 % think that the same should be true for bars and restaurants .
<en> Ladies and gentlemen , waiters and bar staff also have a right to life and to health protection !
<en> Each year 80 000 people die from passive smoking .
<en> Regardless of their own wishes they have breathed in a mixture of 250 carcinogens and toxins .
<en> Waiters in establishments where smoking is allowed are 50 % more likely to contract lung cancer than staff working in smoke-free establishments .
<en> None of this is news .
<en> Yet 30 % of European Union citizens are smokers .
<en> The free market economy has not stopped an unhealthy habit which causes hundreds of thousands of deaths and costs taxpayers billions .
<en> It is clear that lawmakers must act .
<en> I agree with the report that only a 100 % smoke-free environment is an environment which can meet today 's health requirements .
<en> In addition to a ban , however , we also need measures which help smokers free themselves from their addiction .
<en> We need only look at the sums spent by the tobacco industry on advertising to understand the enormity of the challenge we face .
<en> Half-measures are no longer adequate .
<en> It is time to act in earnest .

<en> The next item is the recommendation by Gianluca Susta , on behalf of the Committee on International Trade , on the Protocol amending the TRIPS Agreement ( 08934 / 2006 - C6-0359 / 2006 -

<en> rapporteur . - ( IT ) Mr President , Commissioner , ladies and gentlemen , I would first of all like to take this opportunity to thank the Secretariat of the Group of the Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe in Parliament for the support it has given me .
<en> I would also like to thank all the shadow rapporteurs , as well as Mr Van Hecke , who preceded me in covering this dossier , for the excellent work carried out and for managing to maintain the unity of our institution right through to the end .
<en> In my opinion , this has been Parliament 's greatest strength in the campaign to promote access to medicines in the developing and less-developed countries where they are most needed .
<en> The right to health and access to health at affordable prices are fundamental rights and should be guaranteed for all citizens .
<en> Unfortunately we know only too well that this is not always the case : all too often the prices imposed by the pharmaceutical industry are too high , with the result that countries where they are most needed find themselves in difficulty .
<en> For this reason , as I have already said on several occasions , both in the Committee on International Trade and in plenary , Parliament could not blindly accept the Protocol amending the TRIPS Agreement as if it were a universal panacea , and then consider the matter resolved .
<en> Parliament wanted more to be done , at least within the European Union , because the European Union can and must do more .
<en> Even in the light of the regrettable events of this summer , such as the exchange of letters with Thailand , even if partially resolved , the European Parliament , which has always been a great advocate of using all the flexibilities offered by the TRIPS Agreement , could not give the go-ahead for the ratification of the protocol without obtaining real and effective guarantees from the Commission and the Council .
<en> I think it is fair to stress that during these months of close collaboration with the Commission and the Council , we have undoubtedly achieved an important goal for the European Union , by putting an essentially technical dossier at the top of the European political agenda .
<en> I believe that the end result can be qualified as a success , not only for this reason , but above all because we have succeeded in making progress in extremely sensitive areas , such as encouraging the use of the flexibilities provided for under the TRIPS Agreement so that we can promote access to essential medicines at affordable prices within the framework of national public health programmes .
<en> I particularly support the explicit reference contained in the Council Statement - presented on Monday - to Article 30 of the TRIPS Agreement .
<en> For my group , this represents a guarantee and an assurance that Member States will be able to use this instrument without coming under pressure and that there will be easier access to medicines in countries where they are most needed .
<en> Secondly : I am also delighted at the results obtained in terms of TRIPS-plus , namely the more stringent provisions as regards those provided for under the TRIPS Agreement .
<en> Parliament , the Council and the Commission have agreed that there should be no negotiations in future bilateral or regional agreements with developing countries on provisions that might have negative consequences for health and access to medicines .
<en> Despite this , while recognising the efforts of the Portuguese Presidency , I would like to ask whether the text of the statement can be further improved , particularly in the section referring to poor developing countries .
<en> This expression could create confusion , since it is now customary to refer only to developing countries and to the category of less-developed countries .
<en> To insert a new category would complicate the situation .
<en> Above all , it is important to stress that all developing countries , hence even countries such as Brazil , India , etc . , must be able to use the current system without running the risk of pejorative provisions being introduced in future .
<en> Last but not least , it is vital to underline the efforts made to date in terms of the transfer of research and technological development to southern countries .
<en> The ALDE Group is ready to give its assent because it believes that a ' no ' would send out a negative signal to the countries most in need , and would be irresponsible on the part of the European Union given that the reopening of the WTO negotiations is unrealistic .
<en> However , this does not change the fact that we continue to have reservations about the efficiency of the mechanism studied and approved by the WTO .
<en> For this reason , and I am almost at the end now , I would like to confirm that the EU will not stop here .
<en> Parliament will do everything it can to ensure that the guarantees that have been given over the past few months will be honoured in practice .
<en> Therefore we ask Commissioner Mandelson , who in his letter confirmed that he did not intend to negotiate TRIPS-plus provisions , to remove from the draft Economic Partnership Agreement with the Caribbean countries the request for adherence to and acceptance of the obligations of the Patent Cooperation Treaty , the Patent Law Treaty and the intellectual property provisions of Directive 2004 / 48 / EC on the enforcement of intellectual property rights , which unequivocally resemble TRIPS-plus provisions .
<sp>
<en> Member of the Commission . - Mr President , I am very pleased that we have been able to find a solution agreeable to all on the important issue of access to medicines for poor , developing countries .
<en> Our debate during the last months has been fruitful and I would like to thank Parliament for the intensity and the quality of our exchanges .
<en> The Commission has always been receptive to the concerns expressed by Parliament and , indeed , shares most of them .
<en> That is why the Commission was at the forefront of the debate on TRIPS and access to medicines in the WTO .
<en> I have seen in this debate an opportunity for the Commission to clarify its position on a number of issues .
<en> We all agree that the amendment of the TRIPS agreement is one part of the solution among many others to the problem of access to medicines .
<en> Obviously , other measures are needed , in particular to improve health care systems and the infrastructures , notably in poor , developing countries .
<en> Some Members fear that the mechanism will not work .
<en> This is certainly too early to assert .
<en> In our regulation implementing the waiver , and together with Parliament , we agreed to evaluate it three years after its entry into force , and we will do it .
<en> We also support the work of the intergovernmental working group with the WHO to explore other measures to further improve access to medicines .
<en> The Commission has been able to reaffirm its attachment to the Doha declaration on the TRIPS agreement on public health and its support for the flexibilities contained therein .
<en> Similarly , this debate allows me to dispel any misunderstanding about what the Commission is doing in the economic partnership agreements with ACP countries .
<en> Let me confirm that , in those agreements and in other future bilateral and regional agreements with poor developing countries , the Commission is not asking and will not ask for provisions which could affect access to medicines or undermine the TRIPS flexibilities contained in the Doha declaration on the TRIPS agreement and public health .
<en> Thanks to this frank and direct debate Parliament is now in a position to give its assent to the Commission proposal .
<en> The European Community will then join the other WTO members which have already accepted the TRIPS agreement .
<en> This acceptance will enable the EC to continue to play a leading role in the WTO on the issue of access to medicines .
<en> To conclude , I would like to insist that access to medicines remains a priority for the Commission and I am willing to continue to work in a constructive spirit with Parliament on this matter in the future .

<en> ( PL ) Madam President , the problem of effective enforcement of monetary claims across the territory of the European Union is very important in terms of ensuring proper functioning of the internal market .
<en> It is worth considering Community action in this regard .
<en> There is a very important saying that was impressed on me when I was a trainee lawyer , according to which when we do someone a favour we become indebted to them .
<en> This is sometimes true .
<en> Delaying payments or failing to make them altogether endangers the interests of companies and consumers alike .
<en> The differences in the efficiency of debt recovery that currently exist within the European Union can threaten the competitiveness of companies whose activities extend beyond the borders of a particular Member State .
<en> The systems for enforcing orders differ between individual Member States .
<en> In some states they are more effective than in others .
<en> As things stand at present , a debtor may almost instantly transfer funds from accounts known to the creditor to other accounts located in the same country or in another Member State .
<en> This makes it practically impossible for creditors to block those funds .
<en> Furthermore , creditors seeking enforcement of an order in another Member State are confronted with a different legal system and procedural requirements .
<en> The language barrier and cost of the proceedings represent additional obstacles .
<en> I therefore believe that we should respond positively to the proposal to create a European system to attach bank accounts .
<en> Bearing in mind the increasing integration in the Single Euro Payments Area , legal regulation of this type is both appropriate and essential .
<en> I would like to thank Mr Lechner for this report .
<en> I am sure it will represent a turning point in the Union 's legal system .

<en> This European instrument , this European attachment order that is under discussion , really could complement national legislation and hence deal with the serious infringements of creditors ' rights that occur on a transnational basis .

<en> Clearly , as you are all aware , Europe has no unilateral power to act .

<en> ( NL ) Madam President , I am speaking here on behalf of my colleague Mr Blokland .
<en> This debate is a further demonstration that the proposed soil policy is very controversial .
<en> Now that there are two proposals - the strategy and the Directive - it seems as though a new branch of environmental policy is being introduced .
<en> I say ' seems ' , as nothing could be further from the truth .
<en> Sustainable management of soil use already comes to the fore in 33 European directives , such as the Water Framework Directive .
<en> Why , then , are we presenting overlapping legislation , entailing yet more burdens , particularly for Member States that already have a well-functioning soil policy ?
<en> I shall be supporting Mr Prodi 's Thematic Strategy .
<en> In my opinion , Member States who have yet to develop a soil policy must do so on the basis of the strategy .
<en> The framework directive , on the other hand , is disproportionate and also , in my view , contravenes the principle of subsidiarity .
<en> Unlike air and water , soil does not have a cross-border dimension , and policy is often implemented on a regional or local scale .
<en> This is also the reason that I - that is , Mr Blokland - have joined in signing the amendment rejecting the Commission proposal .
<sp>
<en> Madam President , we are familiar with the idea that a land grab is the unwarranted appropriation of property belonging to another .
<en> It seems to me that this soil directive amounts to an unwarranted power grab by Brussels , and of course brings with it an inevitable layer of fresh bureaucracy .
<en> Soil , as has been said in this debate , unlike air and water , does not flow from state to state .
<en> It has no cross-border dimension .
<en> Thus policy on soil is and should remain a Member State issue .
<en> IPPC , cross-compliance obligations , the Landfill Directive and the Nitrates Directive all give us more than enough EU involvement .
<en> Hence I have no apology for favouring total rejection of this power-hungry proposal .
<en> But , if , true to form , the EU nonetheless decides to meddle in this national issue , then one initiative it could consider is to introduce a payment to farmers in return for providing carbon sequestration in soil management and farming practices .

<en> ( FR ) Madam President , my first thought on this proposal for a directive was to reject the text .

<en> Why have another text on the protection of soil when we already have a whole raft of regulations on soil , waste , pesticides and the protection of nature ?
<en> Within the framework of better lawmaking , I was thinking that we should not appear to be going through the European Commission mill again .
<en> I was putting myself in the shoes particularly of the mayors of our municipalities , who would find themselves with another text to dissect .

<en> We have worn out the soil with intensive production .
<en> In addition to this there is climate change and desertification .
<en> Our urban planning policies have mineralised the soil , degraded it , and our fellow citizens are now surprised when they experience catastrophic flooding because the soil no longer absorbs the rain .
<en> Who has not seen the open wounds in the landscape caused by the quarries that supply us with such valuable materials ?
<en> Impoverished , dried out , degraded , polluted and bruised soil - that is what has become of this land , which previous generations spoke about with veneration because the land was everything to them : their work , their food , their life and , for many , their only property .
<en> What was once our mother Earth we now regard with suspicion .
<en> What will be the consequences of this degradation , this pollution , for our environment and health ?

<en> She has listened to Parliament .
<en> She has found balanced positions that respect the need for subsidiarity in the choice of methods , because there is enormous disparity between the Member States .
<en> The final text has evolved a great deal .
<en> It avoids increasing the burden of administrative costs by encouraging us to put right the mistakes of the past , our agricultural , industrial and urban practices that did not respect the soil .
<en> This report , completely remodelled by Mrs Guti√©rrez , is satisfactory .
<en> There is such soil diversity in the European Union that the subsidiarity guarantee is essential , while ensuring the protection and sustainable use of the soil .

<en> in writing . - ( PT ) Protection of the environment is a politically important issue in Europe which has developed rapidly in recent years and in which research continues to be a priority for the Union .
<en> However , the environment cannot be protected in Europe without protecting the soil which is exposed to various degradation processes .
<en> The need for specific protection measures within a new European framework in this area therefore makes total sense .
<en> We recognise that , in the main , soil is in private ownership , but also that soil is a natural resource of public interest and therefore must be preserved for the benefit of future generations .
<en> As protection of the soil is closely linked with the main international environmental challenges , there is a need to consider Community legislation which is specifically designed to protect the soil itself and which can encourage the exchange of information and coordination of good practices among the Member States .
<en> Inserting soil protection in a future climate regime therefore seems to presuppose the recognition of the need for greater knowledge about the role of this resource in the mitigation of and adaptation to climate change .

<en> in writing . - ( PL ) Multi-faceted protection of the soil is one of the main challenges for environmental protection at international level .
<en> It also has a tremendous impact on the economies of the Member States .
<en> I wish to express my concern about the consequences of natural degradation of the soil and degradation caused by human activity .
<en> Degradation of the soil is often the result of inappropriate human activity in the areas of agriculture and forestry .
<en> It can also be a consequence of industry , tourism , and urban development .
<en> I should like to point out to the House that compliance with the provisions of the directive will make it possible for degraded land to be reclassified , thus preventing the use of green field sites for industrial and commercial purposes .
<en> The directive will also provide for soil to be classified in terms of its potential for plant and animal production , with particular reference to the production of high quality food .
<en> I should like to highlight the need to develop a European strategy aimed at identifying and resolving issues relating to soil degradation .
<en> Due to the great variety of soil types , a European strategy is required , independently of national action .
<en> Such a European strategy would be based on prevention , and would aim to raise public awareness and to persuade the public of the need for soil protection .
<en> In addition , the strategy would identify risk areas with a view to resolving this problem at European level .
<en> It should be noted that it is important to establish a clear demarcation between this directive and other European legislative standards relating to soil protection in order to avoid regulatory duplication .
<en> Current European legislation does not appear to prevent degradation of the soil .
<en> At the same time , soil protection is closely linked to the main international challenges in the area of protection of the natural environment .
<en> I therefore believe that there is a clear need to develop Community legislation aimed at protecting the soil as such .

<en> on behalf of the PSE Group . - ( FI ) Mr President , my sincere thanks go to the rapporteur Mrs Kallenbach , to the other shadow rapporteurs , and to Mrs McCarthy , Chairman of the Committee on the Internal Market and Consumer Protection , for seeing through this complicated legal package .
<en> When almost two years ago we started this work , we were assured that this would above all be a technical measure , the sole purpose of which was to use the UN Firearms Protocol to enable it to become EU legislation .
<en> The process , however , was anything but a technical one .
<en> Some wanted to ban weapons completely and restrict people 's legal enjoyment of them , whilst certain people did not want to see any kinds of controls on the purchase and use of weapons .
<en> Under the leadership of our rapporteur , Mrs Kallenbach , however , we found a balanced compromise among the main groups , one which takes account of the safety of individuals and society as well as the needs of those who enjoy using weapons as a pastime and hunters too , for example .
<en> It is a good thing that all weapons in the EU should be registered in order to make it easier to trace them and that Member States in future will have to keep the details of a weapon and its owner for a period of 20 years .
<en> It is also important that imitation and converted weapons should be covered under the directive .
<en> The lives of hunters and marksmen will be made a lot easier when the European Firearms Pass is the only document they need when travelling from one country to another , and there should be no fee charged for one .
<en> The age limit of 18 years old which is stipulated in the directive and its exceptions is sensible , in my view .
<en> It means , for example , that in my country , Finland , the thousands of registered underage hunters may continue to pursue their hobby with the permission of their parents , just as they have up until now .
<en> It is directives such as these which prove their worth in the eyes of the public .
<en> The EU 's Four Freedoms will likewise gain strength when the EU is developed as a safe area of internal rights .

<en> King of the Hashemite Kingdom of Jordan . - Bismillah ar-Rahman ar-Rahim , Mr President , Members of Parliament , ladies and gentlemen , thank you for your warm welcome and , on behalf of the people of Jordan , I am honoured to come before this distinguished institution again .
<en> My friends , a changing Europe and a changing Middle East are here today .
<en> A Europe of expanding membership and a visionary mission : for cooperation across borders and growth without barriers .
<en> A Middle East of new horizons and growing hope : for peace among neighbours , opportunities for our people and a future for our youth .
<en> These trends do not take place in isolation .
<en> The achievement of the hopes of our regions will advance stability and create new possibilities for security and prosperity worldwide .
<en> It is deeply in our interest to succeed .
<en> And a critical opportunity is before us .
<en> Two weeks ago , with the support of the European Union and nations from both our regions , Israelis and Palestinians met at Annapolis .
<en> They pledged all-out negotiations toward a peace treaty in 2008 and immediate steps to implement their obligations under the Road Map .
<en> For the first time in years , we see movement towards a permanent settlement and an independent , sovereign , viable Palestinian state .
<en> ( Applause )
<en> This progress is the work of many friends of peace , including leaders in Europe and the Arab states .
<en> We believed that , after years of worsening crisis , a change of strategy was required .
<en> We urged a new commitment to the two-state goal and a targeted process that could achieve it - with tight timelines , measurable requirements and milestones for action .
<en> Second chances are rare , but I believe we have come to one .
<en> Very real challenges lie ahead , but Annapolis has created a new spark of hope .
<en> We can and must fan that spark into a blaze of confidence , action and tangible results .
<en> As our near neighbour , Europe shares our interest in solving this , the central crisis of our age .
<en> All sides respect Europe 's neutral role and model of regional progress and peace .
<en> For years , you have been our partner in the search for solutions .
<en> And you will be our partner , too , in the benefits of success : a vibrant zone of peace and prosperity throughout our shared hemisphere .
<en> These realities give Europe an important and prominent role in the future of peace .
<en> I speak especially of the European Union , and you , the voices of Europe , here in the European Parliament .
<en> And I have come here today to urge your active engagement , to seek your specific , practical skills and investment in the future , and to offer Jordan 's own commitment in the days of work that lie ahead .
<en> My friends , there are major areas where action must begin now .
<en> The first is to support the negotiations and their goal : a final settlement creating an end to conflict , security for both Palestine and Israel , and at long last , a sovereign , independent and viable Palestinian state .
<en> ( Applause )
<en> We must not underestimate the difficult days ahead .
<en> The issues are complex and decades old .
<en> Real grievances must be faced - and left behind .
<en> On the positive side , Israelis and Palestinians understand their deep , shared stake in ending the conflict .
<en> And a great amount of work has already been done .
<en> From Oslo , through the Road Map , through the Geneva Accords , and other initiatives , the parameters of the solutions are in focus .
<en> I believe the parties can get to the endgame .
<en> But for this to happen , it is vital that the international community be engaged .
<en> Europe has a unique experience of the mechanisms and process of post-conflict recovery and reconciliation .
<en> This includes creating a security framework that can offer assurance to both sides .
<en> European peacekeeping forces have played a constructive role in Lebanon .
<en> Your commitment can help bring great trust to a Palestinian-Israeli settlement .
<en> On the ground , there is a need , not only for resources but for partnership - to boost economic opportunities , create confidence that the political process works , and help create the conditions that will sustain peace .
<en> Both Palestinians and Israelis need to see tangible results , and quickly .
<en> That means security from violence and an end to occupation ; but it also means better conditions of life .
<en> In the occupied territories , the humanitarian situation for Palestinians remains dire .
<en> People need access to jobs and education , effective public services and more .
<en> Such action will provide a major infusion of hope and be a powerful counter-argument to extremist predictions that nothing can change .
<en> Next week , donor nations and institutions will meet in Paris to make commitments and plan the way forward .
<en> European nations and the European Union are already providing help , a commitment respected by people throughout the region .
<en> A second and related imperative is to understand and articulate the potential of peace .
<en> We must begin now to re-envision the future : a region where conflict has given way to cooperation , where a regional economy brings together the capabilities and resources of 22 countries - more than 300 million people , from the Atlantic to the Indian Ocean - and where cross-border partnerships advance development , health , the environment and more .
<en> It is a future that empowers people to be full participants in global progress .
<en> And it will unleash a new scope of partnership with our European neighbours , in science , technology and trade .
<en> This promising future is why we must move swiftly on a comprehensive settlement , with action on the Syrian and Lebanese tracks .
<en> Indeed , the entire Arab world has recognized the importance of moving forward .
<en> The Arab peace initiative was affirmed , unanimously , last spring .
<en> And it has received the support of Muslim countries beyond the region .
<en> The opportunity is here , at long last , for a sovereign , independent , and viable Palestinian state and full , normal relations between Israel and 57 Arab and Muslim nations .
<en> This means acceptance ; acceptance by key countries , with billions of citizens , representing almost a third of the membership of the United Nations .
<en> And that opens a shared future of security , peace and new partnerships .
<en> Achieving such a peace will also make a substantial impact on other issues .
<en> Within the region , it will create new strategic space , allowing the resolution of other serious issues , from poverty to proliferation .
<en> Aggressive forces will no longer be able to exploit the Palestinian cause to serve their own ambitions and interests .
<en> ( Applause )
<en> Resources and attention will be freed to advance the region 's potential through development and reform .
<en> We in Jordan are ready to meet that future .
<en> We have pressed forward with our reform programme , despite regional instability .
<en> In the last decade , we have achieved significant gains : strong economic growth , rising per capita incomes , and a model education system .
<en> And Europe has been an important partner , through private-sector investments , as well as official assistance .
<en> Allow me to say that we deeply appreciate the support and friendship of this Parliament and the European Union .
<en> ( Applause )
<en> And we believe that in the days after peace , our partnership can only soar higher .
<en> My friends , today we can think of a larger neighbourhood , one that stretches from north of the Baltic Sea to south of the Mediterranean , one that is shared by Europe and the Middle East .
<en> It is the basis of the Euromed partnership , our region-to-region platform for cooperation and development .
<en> It is a relationship with great shared interests and unlimited potential .
<en> And it is up to us to develop our partnership to its fullest .
<en> Today , young Europeans are coming to adulthood who never knew a divided Europe .
<en> Their young counterparts , Palestinian and Israeli , have no such positive experience .
<en> They have grown up in a world of division and conflict .
<en> Now , together , we have an opportunity to remove the barriers to their future , and leave the past behind .
<en> Today , the European Parliament represents significantly more Member States than when I spoke before Parliament only five years ago .
<en> That is the result of a region-wide commitment to increase the zone of partnership and progress .
<en> The Middle East is tackling the same important task .
<en> Now , together , we can help that work succeed .
<en> Today , a renewed peace process has begun .
<en> We have seen such beginnings fail in the past .
<en> But this time , a unique confluence of events has created new openings for success .
<en> Now , together , we can and we must , fulfil the promise of peace .
<en> ( Applause )
<en> My friends , we in Jordan know that when an olive tree takes life , planting is only the first step .
<en> A hundred processes are then activated to create the cells and structures of life .
<en> Roots emerge , growth occurs , and a core of strength ensures survival .
<en> From outside comes water and support to sustain life and create new fruit .
<en> In the arena of the Middle East , a new olive branch has just been planted .
<en> Now the real work must begin .
<en> It is in our hands to create the process and structures that will give peace roots , help it grow and sustain it into the future .
<en> I urge you to share in this effort .
<en> Our partnership can create an historic transformation and a rich harvest - years of peace and prosperity that will benefit our peoples and our world .

<2en> This made Montenegro the 49th independent state in Europe .

<en> in writing . - ( PT ) The resolution adopted today in the European Parliament expresses solidarity with the victims of the shipwrecks that occurred in the Kerch Strait - that is , the Strait linking the Black Sea to the Sea of Azov - causing an environmental disaster .
<en> The environmental impact of the spillage of oil derivatives into the strait was exacerbated by the rapid dispersion of the pollutants due to the strong winds and high waves at the time .
<en> In general , we agree with the positions contained in the resolution , stressing the important role of Member States in ensuring that ships on their national registers conform to international standards and in preventing maritime accidents and combating the consequences of such accidents .
<en> Agreeing with the need to implement measures to reduce the environmental risk and to make progress in maritime safety , we think that any initiative taken at EU level in this framework should be based on enhanced cooperation between Member States , without compromising their responsibilities in this area .

<en> I would therefore like to draw particular attention to the role of the EUFOR TCHAD / RCA operation .

<en> author . - Madam President , I want to make a couple of important and essential points .
<en> There is absolutely no doubt that intervention is required in Chad .
<en> There is no doubt that the teeming human misery of refugees in that part of our world is unbearable to see , but I want to state very clearly that there are a number of core difficulties with this proposed mission .
<en> The first of these is the lack of clarity in terms of the operation 's mandate .
<en> We are saying that this is a peace-keeping and humanitarian effort .
<en> If that is indeed so , then this must be made doubly clear in the terms of reference for the troops we send .
<en> I believe that clarity is lacking .
<en> I do not believe - and I have to disagree with my colleague - that an intervention shaped in this way will actually increase security .
<en> We have recently witnessed a growing intensity and barbarity of the conflict .
<en> We have also heard from leaders of many of the rebel groups that any intervention , and this intervention in particular , will be considered hostile .
<en> That poses a huge difficulty .
<en> I must also say - and , again , I disagree with my colleague - that the troops as currently configured will not act as the neutral force that is required .
<en> I have to say , with the greatest of respect for France and her people , that to load the mission so much towards France verges on the provocative , and I think it deeply unwise .
<en> I do not believe that it is possible for us to formulate a common European defence or security policy .
<en> The difficulties that have arisen - in this instance in relation to Chad - reflect very clearly why .
<en> I think it is undoable , because we have very different traditions and histories and very different foreign policy goals and outlooks .
<en> For this reason in particular it is a great shame - if I may say so , coming from a country that is still at least nominally militarily neutral - that the obligations , responsibilities and capacities of militarily neutral states are not recognised sufficiently in the European Union , and particularly not in the Lisbon Treaty .
<en> I believe that countries with that tradition could make the kind of valued intervention based on neutrality that my colleague has mentioned .
<en> To conclude , intervention in Chad is necessary .
<en> However , the essential thing is how we go about this .
<en> Any operation has to be focused .
<en> It certainly has to be neutral and , above all , it must have prospects of success .

<en> on behalf of the ALDE Group . - Madam President , the ALDE Group warmly welcomes the content of Mr Schlyter 's report , which is to be commended for its sensitive , yet highly practical , approach .
<en> Members of the public find it almost impossible to understand just how it is that we can allow fish to be caught and then thrown back dead into the sea .
<en> Fishermen too have major concerns with the fact that this kind of action is , to some extent , forced upon them , for the current combination of rules and technical possibilities means that some fish are simply not wanted on board .
<en> Sometimes this is because they are of insufficient economic value .
<en> We must make an early and concerted effort to prevent the kind of discarding that results from attempts at high grading .
<en> I suspect that there is already less temptation to this practice in those fisheries where days at sea are limited .
<en> Sometimes , though , discarding is the outcome of conditions we ourselves impose , for example minimum landing sizes , and restrictions on quotas .
<en> Of course , if we are serious about conservation , we need total allowable catches .
<en> But , in my own view , we need to look seriously at the methods we employ to keep fishing within the limits that are set by those TACs , to determine amongst other things , just how far there is an interconnection between the establishment of quotas and the problem of discards , particularly where mixed fisheries are concerned .
<en> This , as well as the adoption of the measures suggested in the report , must of course be undertaken with the full engagement of stakeholders .
<en> Without that , we cannot hope for success .
<en> The industry is already leading the way .
<en> I am particularly proud of the Scots , for their voluntary system of real-time closures .
<en> We need proper incentives to positive actions of this kind for a great deal remains to be done .
<en> I trust that Parliament will give its full support to the report and that the Commission and Council will take matters forward in the manner it recommends .
<sp>
<en> on behalf of the UEN Group . - ( GA ) Mr President , I should like to say that I approve of this report ; to my mind , the rapporteur has worked out a practical , comprehensive approach to the problem of fisheries discards at sea .
<en> But things are not so easy , and everyone is thinking about the new methods to be applied .
<en> It is time to put an end to the volumes of talk about this matter and take action .
<en> There are plenty of practical suggestions in the report and they could be put into operation .
<en> The one thing that we definitely cannot do is to do nothing .
<en> We have to act for as long as fisheries discards pose a problem .
<en> I should also like to ask the Commission ensure that small fishermen do not incur any additional cost on account of measures to resolve the problem of these discards .
<sp>
<en> on behalf of the Verts / ALE Group . - Madam President , the common fisheries policy ( CFP ) has been a miserable failure .
<en> It has failed to conserve stocks , it has failed to sustain our fishing-dependent communities and it has failed to win public support or credibility .
<en> One of the main reasons for that is the scandal of discarding .
<en> The CFP quota system itself is a direct cause of discarding .
<en> It does not measure the amount of fish caught ; it only measures the amount of fish landed .
<en> That said , I broadly welcome this report by Mr Schlyter .
<en> In particular , I strongly agree with the principle of positive incentives giving some reward to those fishermen who take steps to reduce or eliminate discards .
<en> I also agree that measures must be tailored to different types of fishery .
<en> It has long been a major flaw of the CFP that it has been over-centralised and inflexible .
<en> I draw attention to paragraph 15 , which welcomes the voluntary real-time closure scheme introduced by Scotland , an excellent example of the kind of initiative which should be encouraged and incentivised by the CFP at least for as long as we are stuck with it as a management measure .
<sp>
<en> on behalf of the IND / DEM Group . - Madam President , discards are just one aspect of the nightmare that is the CFP .
<en> The EU , through its ill thought-out policy , is destroying livelihoods in developing nations across the world .
<en> The export of fish is significantly more important to the developing world in trade terms than other commodities such as rice , coffee and tea .
<en> Mauritania , for example , is dependent on its fishing industry for half of its exports , which represent 15 % of its GDP .
<en> But , having devastated Mauritanian waters , the Commission now wants to dump its deal .
<en> It does not think that these now sterile waters are worth EUR 86 million a year .
<en> This denunciation of a fisheries agreement is supposed to be a secret ; well , it was until now .
<en> I think African people should know about the EU 's shabby and dishonourable plans .
<en> It is colonialism at its most vicious , and I accuse these institutions of racism and exploitation of vulnerable societies .
<en> President Barroso 's non-imperial empire is not as benign as he would have us believe , so , if you want to move forward , discard Giscard and dump the Lisbon Treaty as well as the CFP .
<sp>
<en> Madam President , the scandal of discards is one of the EU 's own making .
<en> Impossible quotas and restrictions are imposed in mixed fisheries , prohibited stocks are inevitably caught and in consequence they are dumped back - dead - into the sea .
<en> And all this while hunger prevails in many parts of the world .
<en> For years the EU has wrung its hands over this but , frankly , has done nothing to stop it .
<en> Such fish , I believe , should be landed ; they should be sold at a fixed price , sufficiently low to discourage deliberate catching and sufficiently high to make their landing worthwhile .
<en> Also , it is sensible and right that we should reward the use of more selective fishing gear .
<en> But I do most positively reject any blanket discard ban as translating into yet another device of driving more of our fishermen out of business .
<en> We have ruminated on this issue for years .
<en> Now is the time , at last , to do something about it .

<en> Mr President , in the lead-up to the Beijing Olympics , the focus of the international community is on China 's record for violations of human rights .
<en> However , we must not forget that other species , primarily the tigers , are suffering too .
<en> Their numbers are being devastated due to huge demand - largely from China - for tiger-related products .
<en> The cause of their looming extinction is the illegal poaching of tigers in India .
<en> Even in reserves , keepers have been shot to get at the tigers .
<en> These are then illegally transported across the border to China .
<en> It is estimated that one tiger is killed every day .
<en> At this rate the tiger will be virtually extinct within the next five years .
<en> I welcome the news last week that the Indian Government plans to create eight new reserves to protect their dwindling population of tigers .
<en> Nevertheless , it will take five years to set up new reserves , and in the last five years the population of tigers has already dropped by over 50 % .
<en> Therefore , unless the European Union and international community take urgent action in curbing demand and tackling illegal poaching and trafficking , and changing attitudes in China on tiger-related products , the new reserves will be too little too late .
<en> Finally , I hope you will support me on Tiger Protection Awareness Day .

<en> ( PL ) Mr President , last week the Polish media reported the story of Karolina , a young girl whose life has been ruined by her former boyfriend .
<en> Without her knowledge or consent , the boyfriend recorded their shared private experiences and posted the recordings on the Internet after the end of their relationship .
<en> Karolina 's family and friends received e-mails containing pornographic material .
<en> As she is not a minor , Karolina is not protected under Polish law and the perpetrator of this action remains unpunished .
<en> The Polish authorities have undertaken to change the law at the earliest opportunity , so as to protect individuals whose privacy and dignity have been violated in this way .
<en> The Internet transcends national borders , however , and there is no common Union legislation to deter potential perpetrators and penalise those who commit actions of this kind .
<en> I appeal to the Commission and to the Member States to combat such behaviour , which could be described as rape over the Internet .

<en> Member of the Commission . - Mr President , my point of departure is that I am not only pleased but also very proud that we have reached this point , because I agree with all those speakers who consider it a very great achievement for the Union as a whole .
<en> First of all , I would like to express my thanks for your support for the Modernised Customs Code and for your interest in future developments .
<en> As you have recalled , the adoption and subsequent entry into force of the Code will not be the end of the story , since its application will depend on the finalisation and application of its implementing provisions .
<en> The new regulatory procedure with scrutiny will be used for the adoption of these provisions .
<en> It will give Parliament the possibility to check the way the Commission intends to implement in detail , with the assistance of the Customs Code Committee , the general provisions resulting from the Code .
<en> Besides this procedural requirement , the Commission intends to keep Parliament , through its Committee on the Internal Market and Consumer Protection , properly informed about the state of preparation of the draft implementing measures and the time-schedule envisaged for the application of the Modernised Customs Code .
<en> Concerning the problem of Switzerland and the European Union , which Mr Schwab raised , on 1 July 2009 the security amendment to the Community Customs Code will be fully implemented .
<en> This means that all goods entering or leaving the Community shall be the subject of a pre-arrival or pre-departure declaration .
<en> The Authorised Economic Operator will benefit from the facilitations envisaged in the Code .
<en> As with other third countries , we are currently negotiating with Switzerland on the mutual recognition of control centres , the results of controls and the status of Authorised Economic Operator .
<en> The negotiations are ongoing , and we are looking for a mutually satisfactory solution to be in place by 1 July 2009 .
<en> Now let me finish by inviting you to join the celebrations of the 40th anniversary of the Customs Union on 1 July 2008 .
<en> The Customs Union was the first cornerstone in building the internal market and remains one of its essential components .
<en> I am looking forward to continuing our discussion about the future role of customs in the context of the celebrations .
<en> Thank you very much , once again , for your support .

<en> Madam President , a partnership between the EU and Central Asia is long overdue , and I congratulate Mr √ñzdemir on his report .
<en> This vast and strategically vital region is being pulled three ways : by China , by Russia and by Europe .
<en> It is essential that we do all we can to ensure that central Asia 's rational choice is partnership with the European Union .
<en> Turkmenistan 's gradual emergence from isolation provides the EU with a crucial window of opportunity .
<en> Ensuring regular , reliable supplies of ample Turkmen hydrocarbon resources will diminish Europe 's current overdependence on Russia .
<en> This will require a new trans-Caspian pipeline to link up with the Nabucco project .
<en> Uzbekistan , which was rightfully ostracised following the Andijan massacre , has begun to engage in dialogue on human rights with the EU .
<en> This is a considerable step forward .
<en> Clearly there is much progress still to be made before Uzbekistan can be considered a properly democratic country .
<en> However , Uzbekistan is a vital ally in the war on international terrorism , especially with regard to Afghanistan .
<en> For the EU , Kazakhstan should be considered the jewel in the crown of central Asia .
<en> The country 's vast oil , gas and mineral resources , including uranium , are an obvious attraction .
<en> Although Kazakhstan is not a western liberal democracy in our tradition , it is making considerable progress as a multi-religious , secular , Muslim-majority country .
<en> Given the fact that only 17 years ago it was a republic of the Soviet Union , Kazakhstan 's presidency of the OSCE in 2010 will further consolidate the momentum towards greater political freedom and human rights in that country .
<en> As rapporteur of the eastern dimension of the ENP , I once suggested that Kazakhstan might one day become a member of the ENP .
<en> I believe that something rather like this arrangement , one day , will come to pass .

<en> in writing . - In this report on the Treaty of Lisbon we clearly see that the Treaty will bolster the democratic credentials of the EU .
<en> With greater involvement from both National and European Parliaments in decision-making procedures , we are giving the European people what they have always asked of the EU : a greater voice .

<2en> The hallmark of the draft Constitution voted down by two Member States in 2005 was that it responded to the desires of big business , national governments and the majority in national parliaments , but had little support among voters .
<2en> The referendums in the few countries that held one revealed that intense public debate and high turnout lead to many dissenting votes .
<2en> People do not want Europe imposing decisions on them that they themselves would never have wanted to take .
<2en> They do see Europe as useful in resolving cross-border problems peacefully and in tackling large-scale problems that individual Member States cannot solve alone , but they do not see the use of a Europe that increasingly takes the place of the country in which they live .
<2en> The Constitution was a case of tied selling of good and bad things , without the opportunity to edit out the bad points in the fields of the economy and armament .
<2en> The new Treaty still bears a strong resemblance to the Constitution .
<2en> Rejection of referendums reflects fear of the electorate .
<2en> The adoption of the amended Constitution by a clear majority today conveys a clear message : ' People keep out ; this Europe is for professional politicians only ' .

<en> in writing . - ( DE ) The Lisbon Treaty will make a militaristic Europe possible .
<en> Previous EC and EU treaties do not allow a permanent EU military budget , but the ' start-up fund ' ( Article 28 paragraph 3 ) now pays for operational EU military spending .
<en> In addition to the individual states ' military budgets , it provides for the EU to have a military budget of its own .
<en> Article 28c paragraph 3 contains the much-criticised mutual aid and assistance obligation to be implemented via a European Defence Agency ( Article 28 ) .
<en> Institutional collaboration between the EU and NATO is stipulated in the Treaty ( Article 28a paragraph 7 ) .
<en> The right of the Bundestag to decide whether the German Federal Army will be deployed in other countries is significantly undermined .
<en> The Reform Treaty allows for the formation of a military core Europe via ' permanent structured cooperation ' .
<en> This creates a primary legislation framework for increased deployment of EU battle groups ( Article 28 , Protocol 4 ) .
<en> The European Court of Justice is explicitly not competent ( Article 11 , 240a ) .
<en> Nor is the European Parliament competent ; it is merely kept up to date ( Article 21 ) .
<en> This releases future military intervention from democratic control .
<en> This enabling of a militaristic Europe is accompanied by repressive partitioning off of the external borders .
<en> The new Article 62 of the Reform Treaty is designed to effect ' the gradual introduction of an integrated management system for external borders ' .
<en> Thanks to the undemocratic enforcement of the Lisbon Treaty by circumventing referendums , the codifying of neoliberal economic policies and the militaristic parts of the document , Europe is developing in completely the wrong direction .

<en> ( RO ) We have here a very good report , which seems to have said everything .
<en> We thank those who worked on it .
<en> Nevertheless , allow me a reformulation that is not a figure of speech .
<en> Our general goal , as politicians , is to arrange relationships between people in the society , so that we can all live as long as possible keeping harmony between us and nature .
<en> If we accept this goal , we have no demographic problem .
<en> In fact , we are subject to a demographic study only by an unjustified simplification and ignorance of what we are .
<en> There are other indicators measuring the situation of people , as population , and we know them .
<en> They are called human development indexes .
<en> From this point of view , the European Union countries are ranked at the top of the most advanced countries , which is good .
<en> The challenge is not to change the demographic behaviours , but to accept that we need to change our economic and social model .
<en> It is superior to other models , but inadequate .
<en> It lagged behind our own development as people .
<en> There is a gap between our general goal and the organization of the social environment and the economic relations , between declaration and facts .
<en> We say it is necessary to have more children born .
<en> In the meantime , 30 % of Europe 's children live below the poverty threshold .
<en> We ask women to give birth to children , but single mothers experience the biggest risk of exclusion .
<en> The employment rate has to increase , but social services should not be financed .
<en> We export problems and we want to import solutions , but citizens are not a market .
<en> We have to humanize the economic and social relations if we want to solve this problem .
<en> This is the big challenge .

<en> ( HU ) Mr President , I am addressing you now on behalf of a region in demographic crisis and one of the sickest nations in that region .
<en> As a Member responsible for public health , I cannot emphasise strongly enough how closely our demographic problems are linked to public health problems .
<en> In my homeland , Hungary , more people die from cancer than anywhere else in Europe , and this too is contributing to the fact that each year 50 % more people die than are born .
<en> The Castex report on the demographic future of Europe rightly points out that a new policy must be drawn up in the interests of renewal .
<en> Allow me to give just one example : whilst the population of Islamic countries will grow to 1 300 million by 2050 , Europe will fall from 495 to 400 million .
<en> This new demographic policy must be built on two bases : the family , as the most important basic unit of society , and healthy people .
<en> Families must be guaranteed a system that encourages them effectively , and protection .
<en> Today , in many Member States , having children is equal to having poverty .
<en> But there are many good examples too .
<en> There are some countries where the state takes the additional burden from the shoulders of large families .
<en> This good example must be implemented everywhere .
<en> Health is a condition for quality of life .
<en> Citizens must be made interested in preserving their own state of health .
<en> They will obtain the state support necessary for this in every material area , such as compulsory screening tests and free sports opportunities , and all along intellectual lines , that is , with education in health and demographic knowledge .
<en> It is in the fundamental interests of every Member State to improve its demographic and health situation .
<en> This is particularly important in Hungary , where the population might fall below 10 million in future , and where the average life expectancy is ten years lower than the European average .
<en> The future of Europe depends on the demographic performance of the generations living now .
<en> What a government fails to do today with a bad policy will be difficult to rectify later .
<sp>
<en> ( SK ) Ladies and gentlemen , people in the European Union are living longer and longer .
<en> That is a positive phenomenon .
<en> On the other hand , there is a steady decrease in the number of young people .
<en> The number of people in the productive age group will start to fall within no more than three or four years .
<en> Today the ratio is three people of working age to one person of pension age ; it will be just one and a half people of working age in 2050 .
<en> How do we solve the economic effects of the ageing of the population ?
<en> Firstly : we must find jobs for more people .
<en> The traditional policy of men working and women carrying out family duties is not creditable any more .
<en> Most women wish both to become mothers and to have a professional career .
<en> Public policies must back both wishes .
<en> The Scandinavian countries are a good example .
<en> Their active labour market policies combined with better care for women with children offer the best quality of life .
<en> Secondly , we must reform the social welfare systems designed to care for older people and for people who have reached pension age .
<en> If we do not do this on the grounds of social equality and solidarity , the losers will be mostly older people .
<en> In order to achieve a long-term improvement , we need reforms of pension systems and medical care systems , and investment in good health .
<en> Older people have accumulated a lot of knowledge and experience and we need to motivate them to continue to work for longer in their lives .
<en> Ladies and gentlemen , the Lisbon Strategy is beginning a new cycle , giving us an opportunity to introduce reforms that will increase productivity at work and help to create jobs , thus helping to reduce the economic impact of population ageing .

<en> ( RO ) Ladies and gentlemen , at present , Europe is dealing with substantial demographic challenges that will have a long-term impact on its future .

<en> Of all the report 's recommendations , I consider that 3 ideas should constitute the core of the European demographic policy .

<en> The achievement of these objectives unquestionably depends on the level of education and lifelong training of all the generations .
