<en> Member of the Commission . - Mr President , I completely agree with Mr Nicholson that this is the first step in a discussion that is going to continue for almost the rest of this year and , therefore , I shall not go into detail on all the various questions that have been raised here today .
<en> I shall just pinpoint a few of the more important ones .
<en> First of all , a huge majority is in favour of the idea of more decoupling , and I am very appreciative of this idea .
<en> The idea of giving a Member State the possibility to introduce a regional model is a chance for them to go further towards a flat rate and I have explained on various occasions why I think this is important .
<en> In order not to raise any expectations , I will be very direct and very frank on tobacco decoupling .
<en> It was decided in the reform of 2004 to decouple tobacco payments .
<en> As we are now trying to go even further in decoupling , the idea that some of you raised of extending the coupled payment for tobacco would be a step in totally the wrong direction .
<en> Therefore , do not have any expectations that the Commission will move in that direction .
<en> Ms McGuinness said that modulation was like robbing farmers .
<en> I do not agree with this approach .
<en> I think the rural development policy will need more money in order to meet the new challenges - climate change and the reduction of CO2 emissions will be the most important ones .
<en> We have to take into account , firstly , that the decoupled money will stay in the Member States and , secondly , that modulated money is co-financed by Member States and therefore you actually steer the money .
<en> You get twice as much as you deduct from the direct payment .
<en> This is an important message and we will come back to this in the legislative proposals .
<en> Mr Graefe zu Baringdorf mentioned progressive modulation and the necessity , from his point of view , to include labour intensity in these discussions .
<en> I understand his point of view , but I can only say that this will be extremely bureaucratic and very , very difficult to manage , so I am very reluctant to enter into this discussion .
<en> I might be wrong , but , personally , I do not consider the introduction of codecision on agriculture a threat , as I heard suggested .
<en> I consider this a huge and natural step in a situation where the agricultural sector is so important , both from an economic point of view and because this is important for quite a lot of people .
<en> Therefore , I welcome this change , but , on the other hand , it is important that we finalise this health check before the end of the year , otherwise it will be a Health Check for 2010 and then we are too close to 2013 .
<en> That is the reason why , but , believe me , I am very happy with the changes that have been mentioned .
<en> Concerning developing countries , the European Union is the most open market for developing countries : we import more agricultural products than Canada , the United States , Australia and Japan put together .
<en> This has to be taken into account when we talk about the agricultural sector .
<en> I should like to say to Ms Harkin that I have been informed that she has tabled an oral question .
<en> This will be answered in writing and , therefore , I am quite sure she will get all the information she has been asking for .

<en> in writing . - ( HU ) I would like to draw attention to the fact that while women represent approximately 4-5 % of the prison population in Europe , and while the proportion of women in prisons in many European countries is growing at a faster rate than the male prison population , prisons themselves continue to be designed primarily for men and tend to ignore the particular problems of the growing female prison population .
<en> The areas that give greatest cause for concern are healthcare , the situation of mothers with children , and professional and social reintegration .
<en> Statistics on female prisoners suggest a generally low level of education and a lack of vocational skills .
<en> If we want female prisoners to be able to reintegrate into society and have a more stable life following their time in prison , we need to provide all prisoners with opportunities to acquire basic educational skills .
<en> In many European prisons , a difference can be observed between the vocational training offered to women and the demands of the labour market .
<en> Most prisons offer feminised vocational training that is limited to developing the skills and abilities relating to the cultural and social roles traditionally attributed to women .
<en> The labour market does not generally value these low-paid vocational skills highly , and this may favour the perpetuation of social inequalities and undermine social and professional reintegration .
<en> Prison authorities should therefore be encouraged to offer , perhaps in cooperation with external providers , high-quality vocational training measures and varied employment opportunities that are in line with labour market requirements and free from gender stereotypes .

<en> The next item is Question Time ( B6-0019 / 2008 ) .
<en> The following questions have been submitted to the Commission .
<en> Part I
<sp>
<en> Subject : Exchange of information relating to bank accounts
<en> The recent tax scandal in Liechtenstein had repercussions in many Member States of the EU .
<en> According to investigations by the competent authorities , citizens of the Member States are allegedly involved in tax evasion .
<en> I am informed that the Finance Ministers of the 27 Member States urged the responsible Directorate-General of the Commission to carry out a rapid investigation and propose a revision of the legal framework to permit the exchange of information relating to citizens ' bank accounts .
<en> How will citizens ' personal data be protected under such a framework whilst introducing transparency and preventing the transfer and laundering of illicit funds ?
<en> What procedure will the Commission propose to ensure that the ' opening ' of bank accounts is achieved with the greatest respect for legality ?
<en> In what way is it envisaged that Member States ' taxation systems will be harmonised in order to avoid similar situations in the future whereby illicit funds are laundered through bank accounts ?
<sp>
<en> Vice-President of the Commission . - ( DE ) Mr President , ladies and gentlemen , we have to combat tax evasion .
<en> If we do not do this , the basis of our democratic society may erode .
<en> Every nation has the right to enact regulations to ensure that taxes are imposed efficiently with the assent of the people 's representatives .
<en> Individual measures in this sector , however , frequently do not have the desired effect nationally .
<en> International cooperation is therefore required between the tax authorities , involving the exchange of information on bank accounts .
<en> The Finance Ministers of the 27 Member States are working together on this at EU level .
<en> Some measures have already been introduced at European level .
<en> Council Directive 2003 / 48 / EC on taxation of savings income in the form of interest payments is of particular note here .
<en> In addition , the European Union has concluded agreements with third countries , including Liechtenstein , which pursue the same aim as this Directive .
<en> These agreements guarantee that interest received and paid to EU citizens in these third countries is liable either to income tax in their own Member State or to deduction at source .
<en> Deduction at source can be reimbursed to an individual liable to tax in their Member State of permanent residence if the corresponding income is disclosed for tax purposes .
<en> The Economic and Financial Affairs Council carried out an exchange of views on the application of the Directive on taxation of savings income in the form of interest payments on 4 March 2008 .
<en> As a result of the debate , the Ministers asked the Commission to push ahead with work on a report on the implementation of the Directive since it entered into force on 1 July 2005 .
<en> The report should address the definition of the terms ' payment of interest ' and ' beneficial owners ' .
<en> The question rightly being asked here is to what extent systems for exchanging information are compatible with the protection of personal data .
<en> It may be pointed out in this context that the Community rules on data protection , which also apply in the European Economic Area , give Member States the opportunity to take legislative action .
<en> This action can restrict those concerned in some of their rights , such as the right of access or the right to information , if this is necessary for the protection of important financial or economic interests of the European Union or of a Member State .
<en> This also applies to the areas of finance , budgets and taxation .
<en> Comparable restrictions also apply to the effective implementation of the Third Money Laundering Directive .
<en> The Member States must at all events reasonably ensure that their competent bodies comply with the appropriate EU regulations and national data protection regulations when supplying and processing personal data .
<en> A balance has to be found here between the lawful pursuit of aims in terms of taxation policy and the protection of privacy .
<sp>
<en> ( EL ) Mr President , Commissioner , taxation history is full of bogus bank accounts , which are even more harmful when such scandals come to light in European countries .
<en> When it happens , we merely take note of the event , but each time such an incident is repeated our memories flood back .
<en> Is it your overall view , Commissioner , that the system is in actual fact failsafe ?
<sp>
<en> ( DE ) Vice-President of the Commission . - ( DE ) The honourable Member 's question can be answered with a simple no .
<en> The systems we currently have are not watertight ; we know this .
<en> We are therefore making efforts to improve them .
<en> Specific regulations to combat money laundering are definitely open to improvement and we are also making efforts in cooperation with European countries that are part of the European Economic Area but not part of the European Union to achieve these respective improvements .
<en> The Commission has requested and also received a negotiating mandate from the Council authorising it to negotiate specifically with Liechtenstein with regard to how existing weak spots in the system for combating money laundering and tax fraud can be eliminated .
<en> My hope is that the strong public opinion we have witnessed recently in Europe on this issue will help us to reach the necessary agreements .
<en> We are working hard on this , but as you know , tax issues are extraordinarily sensitive .
<en> Even within the Member States , there is definitely still room for improvement here .

<en> The next item is the report by Manolis Mavrommatis , on behalf of the Committee on Culture and Education , on the White Paper on Sport .
<sp>
<2en> Mr President , Commissioner , ladies and gentlemen , let me first thank the Commission and Commissioner Figeƒæ for their initiative in drawing up the White Paper on Sport and the Pierre de Coubertin Action Plan .
<2en> This is the EU 's first effort to deal with sporting matters .
<2en> May I also thank Commissioner ≈†pidla for being here today in place of Commissioner Figeƒæ , who is travelling outside Europe .
<2en> My thanks also go to my colleagues from the Committee on Culture and Education and to the Committee on Economic and Monetary Affairs , the Committee on Employment and Social Affairs , the Committee on the Internal Market and Consumer Protection , the Committee on Legal Affairs , the Committee on Civil Liberties , Justice and Home Affairs , the Committee on Regional Development and the Committee on Women 's Rights and Gender Equality .
<2en> They have cooperated excellently in drafting the report on the White Paper on Sport .
<2en> In the European Parliament report , the key points of the White Paper were covered by 16 conciliation amendments jointly agreed by all the political groups in the Committee on Culture .
<2en> The main points were also covered by 426 amendments tabled to the lead committee and to the other seven committees , which gave their opinions .
<2en> Doping is once again the focus of attention because there are unfortunate examples of it every year in almost every sport .
<2en> Through the White Paper , the European Parliament seeks to adopt measures allowing athletes not be forced by their heavy schedules to resort to performance- and stamina-enhancing substances .
<2en> In addition , internal and external independent checks on professional associations and sports organisations , as well as educating male and female athletes on the side effects of doping may help to curb this problem .
<2en> Debates have focused on two issues of the financial side of sport .
<2en> The first is sports betting .
<2en> We in the Committee on Culture all agree that the possible deregulation of the gaming and lotteries market will be problematic for the funding of amateur sport so long as the existing system of state betting agencies provides it with considerable income .
<2en> For this reason , the White Paper calls on Member States and the Commission to adopt regulations which ensure that amateur and professional sport is protected from any improper influence relating to betting .
<2en> While continuing to protect the betting market , we are thus increasing transparency , and also guaranteeing the state aid for amateur sport , culture and other social activities .
<2en> The second issue is the sale of media rights .
<2en> As we all know , the 27 EU Member States go about selling television rights for major sporting events in different ways .
<2en> This is especially true of Champions League matches and the UEFA Cup .
<2en> Rights can be sold either individually or collectively , but they are the main source of income for professional sport in Europe .
<2en> Similarly , rights to sports events are a vital source of programme content and income for many media owners .
<2en> Parliament 's report also recognises the importance of fairly redistributing income among sports associations , however small , and between professional and amateur sport .
<2en> The collective sale of media rights , which the Commission presents as incompatible with competition law , is therefore important for the redistribution of income .
<2en> It may thus help to achieve greater solidarity among sports .
<2en> We therefore call on the Commission to recognise collective sales and accept that such practical solidarity among small sports clubs is sanctioned by law .
<2en> Lastly , as we stated in the Belet report on professional football , UEFA and FIFA should reach agreement and work with the agencies of the Commission .
<2en> They must ensure that football is universally accepted by the citizens and Member States of the EU without losing its independence ; it must not overstep the powers conferred on it by the statutes .
<2en> It is important for everyone that UEFA and FIFA recognise in their statutes the right of recourse to common courts .
<2en> We must , of course , accept the principle of self-regulation and the structures of the European model of sport governing the organisation of sports events .
<2en> Let me end by reaffirming the satisfaction we all feel at the official recognition of sport by the Member States in the reformed Lisbon Treaty .
<2en> We do of course recognise and respect the special nature of sport .
<2en> It is of great significance for Member States and the sporting world in general that the EU will in future be able to substantially contribute to and promote European policy on sport .
<sp>
<en> Member of the Commission . - ( CS ) In the first place I should present apologies from my colleague Commissioner Figeƒæ , who cannot take part in this sitting because of a long-planned working visit to Egypt .
<en> I accepted the proposal that I should deputise for him with pleasure , inter alia because much of what falls within my competence is closely related to sport .
<en> I would like to thank the rapporteur for the excellent report that he and his colleagues in Parliament have spent six months preparing .
<en> I am convinced that the report is a balanced document and deals with all the relevant themes .
<en> Thank you for the European Parliament 's support for the White Paper on Sport and for your high level of cooperation with the European Commission .
<en> As the European Parliament has emphasised , it is important to recall the principle of the applicability of Community law to sports in Europe , whilst also respecting the specific nature of sport .
<en> Therefore the European Commission remains active on sport , and from now on will apply Community law , including the competition rules , to that area .
<en> The White Paper and its annexes are useful aids for sporting organisations and for Member States in the concrete application of the acquis communautaire to decisions in the area of competition and to judgments of the European Court of Justice .
<en> On the question of the specific nature of sport , the European Commission will lead and support open dialogue with sports organisations , Member States and the European Parliament within the framework of the structured dialogue on sport .
<en> This dialogue will be conducted in such a way that issues of the specific characteristics of sport will be dealt with concretely .
<en> The European Commission does not have any general objections to the amendments to be discussed at this plenary session , especially if their aim is to preserve the proper and equal participation of representative structures in controlling sport .
<en> However , we cannot agree with an unconditional obligation for young players to sign their first professional contract with the club that has trained them , because this infringes the fundamental freedom of free movement of workers .
<en> Meanwhile , as you know , the implementation of the White Paper is continuing according to plan .
<en> Twenty-six of the 53 actions in the Pierre de Coubertin Action Plan have already been carried out ; this year , for example , three studies will be initiated ( with results in 2009 ) , on the following themes : sports funding , players ' agents , and volunteering in sport .
<en> In autumn last year , under the leadership of my colleagues , Commissioner Frattini and Commissioner Figeƒæ , a conference took place on the high level of violence in sport , which identified concrete methods that could achieve an improvement in combating this phenomenon .
<en> The results of measuring the impact of sport on the economy can also be viewed as a significant success .
<en> As far as the matter of ' home-grown players ' is concerned , a short time ago the European Commission was handed the results of an independent expert report analysing UEFA 's rules .
<en> The European Commission is at this very moment examining the compatibility of these rules with Community law .
<en> New possibilities for funding sport and physical activities have also been opened up by various EU programmes , especially the lifelong learning programmes ' Youth in action and ' Europe for citizens ' .
<en> We hope that the Lisbon Treaty will soon come into force and we are delighted with the European Parliament 's support for the preparatory actions in the field of sport , which contribute to implementation of the new EU competence in this area .
<en> Allow me to thank you once again for your contribution , support and splendid cooperation in this important , sensitive and very popular area .
<sp>

<en> draftsman of the opinion of the Committee on Women 's Rights and Gender Equality . - ( SV ) Mr President , let me say a big thank you to the Commissioner , Meglena Kuneva , and rapporteur Lasse Lehtinen .
<en> I welcome the strategy and am very glad that consumers are being treated as an important group to look after .
<en> We know that we shall never get a flourishing internal market unless we have satisfied and secure consumers .
<en> But I share the rapporteur 's view that the strategy calls for continuous follow-up if it is really to develop to the consumers ' advantage .
<en> As rapporteur for the strategy in the Committee on Women 's Rights and Gender Equality , however , I am disappointed that the main reporting committee did not take account of more than one of our 13 amendments .
<en> They contain many important and worthwhile proposals .
<en> We wanted to see a clearer gender perspective .
<en> Consumer policy is definitely not gender-neutral .
<en> Gender should be taken into account just as children , the elderly and the disabled are taken into account .
<en> I hope that this can be taken up again in the next review .
<sp>
<en> on behalf of the PPE-DE Group . - Mr President , my thanks to Mr Lehtinen and to the shadow rapporteurs for the good cooperation over the last few months .
<en> This report introduces some very positive elements in the area of consumer policy moving forward .
<en> Consumers can only exercise their rights if they are aware of those rights , and empowerment of consumers in the EU is a central element of this report , and this will be achieved through education and awareness campaigns .
<en> Special focus will be given to equip consumers with the skills and tools needed to increase their confidence in the digital environment .
<en> The report commends the Commission 's efforts to strengthen cooperation in the area of product safety and at international level , in particular with Chinese and US authorities .
<en> Continued dialogue and information-sharing on product safety is in the interest of all parties and is central to building consumer confidence .
<en> In relation to consumer redress , together with my PPE-DE colleagues I strongly support easy and effective access to redress for all consumers in the EU .
<en> We know that non-judicial forms of redress are the preferred solution of most consumers as they serve consumers ' interests most rapidly at the lowest possible cost .
<en> As I have stated since the outset of discussions , I do not support calls for legislative action to introduce an ill-thought-out system of collective redress in the EU .
<en> The Commission is currently preparing various studies on existing systems of consumer redress in the Member States and rather than pre-empt the results of the Commission studies I , together with my PPE-DE colleagues , call for a strong role for Parliament and the Member States in assessing the results of the studies before deciding upon further action .
<en> It is not in consumers ' interests to hastily introduce a system of collective redress which would be both costly and ineffective .
<en> In all other respects I support the report .
<sp>
<en> on behalf of the PSE Group . - ( DE ) Mr President , Commissioner , may I express my thanks to Mr Lehtinen for the really good draft report he has given us , which provides us with a very sound basis for our discussions .
<en> I should like to highlight three very important points from this report .
<en> The first is the need to ensure that a leading role is played by instruments which we already possess in the European Union for the promotion of safety and prevention .
<en> This is why it is very important that the RAPEX system should be further improved so that it can serve the interests of consumers even more effectively .
<en> The second very important point is that Solvit , which is such a key instrument , should be nurtured and improved .
<en> There is still a very considerable information gap among consumers , too many of whom have never heard of Solvit and do not know that it could resolve a good few problems for them .
<en> That is also very important .
<en> I am also very gratified that the European Commission is to examine the EE symbol again .
<en> Many people believe that the EE symbol is a safety mark , but unfortunately it is not .
<en> We should ensure , together with you and Commissioner Verheugen , that the rules governing this symbol are formulated so as to enable us to assure the public in future that they can rely on the safety of products bearing the EE mark .
<en> That is a very important aim .
<en> The last and most important point , however , in the view of my group is the system of collective redress that we in the Socialist Group are advocating .
<en> The entire statute book serves no purpose if consumers cannot assert their enshrined rights , be it because there is a cross-border dimension which makes the law very difficult to enforce or because there are many small claims for minor losses , although these can certainly suck people dry over time .
<en> It is absolutely essential that we not only encourage the European Commission to examine and develop such a system but actually urge it to do so and to present us with an appropriate piece of draft legislation as soon as possible so that we can really give consumers due security and protection .
<en> I very much regret that the PPE-DE Group has not seen fit to advocate this system with the vigour and commitment that are needed to give consumers and the public at large real confidence in the European Union and the internal market , for such confidence comes from knowing that they are properly protected when they go shopping in Europe .
<sp>
<en> on behalf of the ALDE Group . - ( DE ) Mr President , may I begin by congratulating Lasse Lehtinen on this good and balanced draft report .
<en> We are in agreement on very many points .
<en> One reason for this has been the very good preliminary work of the Commission in this case .
<en> There are few contentious points .
<en> Consumer strategy will be one of the main topics of discussion during the next stage in the development of the internal market .
<en> At the heart of the three main challenges facing the European Union , namely growth , employment and the recognition and satisfaction of people 's needs , are 490 million consumers .
<en> The internal market has the potential to become the world 's largest retail market .
<en> This is why the ALDE Group supports the Commission 's targeted efforts to create one large retail market out of 27 mini-markets .
<en> We also welcome the way in which the draft reinforces the horizontal element of consumer policy as well as its proposal for the appointment of what it calls consumer-liaison officers .
<en> In this context I should make special mention of the proposed strengthening of the European Consumer Centres and the particular attention given to the needs of children and elderly people .
<en> May I also say something on the subject of collective redress , with which we have a problem .
<en> We have had little information and much dogma .
<en> I believe it would be premature , Meglena , to say that you will have the solid backing of Parliament on this matter .
<en> We have just heard from the PPE-DE Group that it will not back you .
<en> I believe the PPE-DE is failing to recognise the real problems .
<en> There is a scatter-gun type of damage that affects many consumers in more than one country .
<en> It is legitimate for the Commission to give some thought to this whole matter and examine it in a study .
<en> On the other hand we have PSE dogma , which craves this instrument at all costs as a political tool , regardless of the real problems - and the real problems are manifold .
<en> There is , for example , the problem of the legal basis .
<en> Where in the Treaty does it say that we here in the Commission and Parliament are entitled to interfere with the Member States ' codes of civil and criminal procedure ?
<en> What did Diana Wallis just tell us on behalf of the Committee on Legal Affairs ?
<en> The problem of contract law is still unresolved .
<en> The question of opting in or opting out , the role of the Ombudsman - there are many problems to resolve .
<en> It is simply not enough to say we do not want the US system .
<en> The Americans also had the best of intentions when they first created their system .
<en> It goes without saying that they did not intentionally create a bad system at the outset .
<en> For these reasons we should maintain an agnostic , critical position .
<en> We should wait for the study , take its findings seriously and then engage in an informed , non-dogmatic and responsible discussion , as befits this Parliament .
<sp>
<en> on behalf of the UEN Group . - ( PL ) Mr President , Mr Lehtinen 's report deals with the major issues of pro-quality strategy for the coming years .
<en> That strategy is important for the citizens of the Union , and I want to stress some of the problems involved .
<en> In the creation of national and EU law there should be greater input from consumer organisations , which are encountering difficulties in pursuing their activities and obtaining funding in certain countries .
<en> The Union should provide more substantive and financial assistance to those organisations .
<en> The collective redress systems applicable in certain countries should be used against dishonest market players , and a collective redress system should be introduced at European level .
<en> European consumer centres in the individual countries , as well as consumer organisations and consumer rights spokesmen , should step up information and education activities aimed at special protection for the most vulnerable consumers .
<en> Protection can be made more effective through the involvement of the Solvit and RAPEX consumer centres .
<en> We support this report .

<en> ( RO ) First of all , I would like to congratulate Mr. Lehtinen for the consistent report .
<en> Nevertheless , I would like to make an observation regarding Paragraph 35 of the report .
<en> This paragraph refers to the creation of a European Consumer Ombudsman in the European Ombudsman 's office .
<en> This proposal seems to be a very complicated and not very efficient procedure to me .
<en> First of all , the creation of such a position requires financial resources .
<en> We would have a redistribution of funds between the European consumer protection centres and the potential new Ombudsman .
<en> Secondly , bureaucracy would increase at the level of the European Union .
<en> Last but not least , we would have an overlapping of the newly-created Ombudsman 's tasks and the European consumer protection centres .
<en> I don 't believe that a new instrument would bring more efficiency in solving the complaints filed by European consumers .
<en> But I do think that an efficient and thorough implementation of the legislation would reduce the dissatisfaction related to the internal market operation .
<en> In conclusion , I request the European Commission representatives to take into consideration Paragraph 7 , by which we request the allocation of adequate funds to the consumer organizations across the European Union .

<2en> This is the freedom of knowledge , which would be added to the four fundamental freedoms - the free movement of goods , services , persons and capital .
<2en> This fifth freedom should help speed up the EU 's transition to a modern , creative knowledge economy .
<2en> It would in turn strengthen the knowledge triangle of scientific research , education and innovation within the EU .
<2en> The initiative proposed by the Commission is no doubt a very good one .
<2en> However , no one would argue against the importance of the original four freedoms in increasing employment .
<2en> Nevertheless , it happens that some Member States fail to adhere to EU policy and even breach the legal norms .
<2en> In pursuing protective policy , they prevent the free movement of capital and persons and jeopardise the development not only of their own countries , but of the EU as a whole .
<2en> In my view , the free movement of services will not guarantee the freedom of development of small and medium-sized enterprises .
<2en> Let us not forget Winston Churchill 's observation that if you destroy a free market , you create a black market .
<2en> The Commission and the Member States should realise that we can achieve much more together than by going our separate ways .

<en> on behalf of the UEN Group . - ( PL ) Mr President , the common employment policy for Member States is undergoing a test .
<en> It is increasingly throwing up employment growth programmes for various age groups , taking account of their specific needs and potential and the threat of problems with finding work .
<en> Under the Lisbon Strategy , these programmes above all envisage investment in people and in their education , and better chances in the job market .
<en> A rise in employment by 3.6 million people in 2007 and an anticipated rise in employment by 4.5 million in 2008-2009 is the perceptible result of this policy .
<en> This means that promoting an approach to work that matches the human life cycle , concern for young people not completing their education and for adapting work conditions to family needs , and especially to parental duties , eliminating discrimination in the workplace , particularly in the scope of access to training and other forms of skill refinement , and gradually restricting occupational activity among older people should in future constitute the basis for action in this sphere .

<en> ( ES ) Mr President , I would first like to discuss Mrs ≈¢icƒÉu 's report .
<en> This proposal is key to modernising the occupation of transport operator , through the uniform application of common rules in all Member States to authorise access to that profession .
<en> In this respect I applaud and willingly welcome the Commission 's proposal .
<en> However , I would like to repeat a question that I raised during the debate on this report in the Committee on Transport and Tourism .
<en> It is regarding the term ' good repute ' , which I put forward , and which , in the interests of consensus , I then withdrew and proposed substituting it with ' ethical standards ' .
<en> I am not in any way questioning this requirement ; on the contrary , I agree that it should be required that transport managers should not have any serious criminal convictions or serious sanctions for infringements of Community legislation relating to road transport .
<en> I do , however , advocate changing the term , because we are presuming bad practice in a profession that is a key sector of the European economy , that generates wealth , creates employment and guarantees the mobility of people and goods .
<en> We should think carefully before assuming that someone is not of good repute to pursue an occupation if that is not proven .
<en> Secondly , I would like to highlight the importance of Mr Grosch 's report on common rules for access to the road haulage market .
<en> The proposal for a regulation defines cabotage operations , putting an end to the current legal uncertainty .
<en> It allows up to three consecutive transport operations for an international carriage of seven days .
<en> However , we should go further in order to lift any restrictions on cabotage and achieve greater liberalisation of national markets .
<en> Finally , I applaud the reduction in bureaucracy that this new proposal for a regulation brings in relation to the new simplified formats for the Community licence , copies of this licence and the drivers ' certificates , that will help to reduce the delays caused by roadside checks .
<en> Ladies and gentlemen , we need to make the transport sector more efficient and more competitive .

<en> in writing . - ( SV ) We actually want all the sittings of the European Parliament to be held in Brussels and we want the travelling circus between Brussels and Strasbourg to end as soon as possible .
<en> We have therefore voted for the proposals that the Monday sittings and Thursday afternoon sittings during Strasbourg part-sessions should be discontinued , in the hope that the sittings in Strasbourg will be phased out completely .
<en> The European Parliament should have a single seat and a single place of work .
<en> It is regrettable that there are Member States whose political leaders consider themselves to be strong supporters of the European idea but at the same time will not give an inch when their national interests are at stake .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - I am generally in favour of what is proposed for the 2009 calendar of part-sessions .
<en> However , I believe that amendments requesting an extension of the time spent in Strasbourg would not contribute to the efficient running of the Parliament .
<en> Indeed , efficiency and logic demands that there be one single Parliament seat in Brussels .
<en> My views on this issue are reflected in my vote .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( PT ) We regard as positive the recognition of the environmental and social problems arising from the closure of mercury mines in the Community .
<en> We also regard as positive the acceptance that projects and other initiatives must continue to be supported , based on the available financing instruments , in order to allow affected areas to find viable solutions for the local environment , employment and economic activity .
<en> It has also been agreed that the permit applicant must take the necessary measures , through a financial guarantee or equivalent mechanism , to ensure that the obligations arising from the permit ( including maintenance operations after closure ) shall be fulfilled and that the closure operations shall be carried out .
<en> It has also been approved that industry sectors that gain mercury from the cleaning of natural gas or as a by-product from non-ferrous mining and smelting operations must provide relevant data to the Commission and the competent authorities of the Member States concerned .
<en> The Commission shall make this information publicly available .
<en> We also feel it is right to encourage the provision of technical assistance to developing countries and countries with economies in transition , especially assistance which facilitates the shift towards alternative mercury-free technologies and the eventual phase-out of uses and releases of mercury and mercury compounds .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( FR ) I voted for this report which aims to bring the ban on exports of mercury forward to 15 March 2011 , three months before the date proposed by the Council .
<en> Mercury can be produced by waste recycling ( fluorescent tubes or batteries , for instance ) , cleaning of natural gas or industrial processing of non-ferrous metals .
<en> I am pleased that , in addition to metallic mercury , the ban includes mercury-containing products that cannot be sold or distributed in the European Union , cinnabar ore and mercury compounds .
<en> It is likewise extremely important that compounds used for research and development , in medicines or in analytic processes not be included in the ban , as stated in the report .
<en> Storage must be made secure , as suggested by both the report and the Council .
<en> Mercury waste stored temporarily for more than one year must be kept in deep underground hard rock formations or in above-ground facilities in such a way as to prevent any risk to human health and the environment before it is processed .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - I generally support Dimitrios Papadimoulis ' report on the banning of exports and the safe storage of metallic mercury .
<en> Bringing forward the date of the export ban to 2010 allows for greater coherence with the EU 's overall mercury strategy .
<en> I also support the extension of the types of mercury covered within the ban .
<en> I further feel that , before the ban comes into force , more research is required regarding safe disposal methods for mercury .
<en> I voted in favour of the report .

<en> The next item is the debate on six motions for resolutions on the arrest of political prisoners in Belarus .
<sp>
<en> author . - ( PL ) Today we are once again discussing breaches of fundamental human rights in Belarus .
<en> As usual in such cases , we note what it is that dictators do .
<en> Obviously dictators always battle with organised religion , because , very often , this is the biggest voice that the population has .
<en> They also always battle with the trade unions .
<en> As it happens the trade unions in Belarus are rather weak , so , from this point of view , Lukashenko could seem quite a positive figure , as he does not have anyone to fight against , since they have not yet managed to create trades unions there .
<en> In addition , dictators always fight against the opposition that wants to have democracy .
<en> However , there is one thing we should also bear in mind : we should remember that Belarus is an important neighbour for the European Union in the East and should be treated as such .
<en> We have a certain tendency to treat Russia as the only neighbour to the East and forget about the fact that Belarus should also be a partner for the EU in the East , as it is a large country with great promise .
<sp>
<en> author . - ( CS ) Ladies and gentlemen , Mr Lukashenko 's regime in Belarus deserves to be criticised for using repressive methods , arresting political opponents , using authoritarian governing methods , censorship and isolation of the country .
<en> In addition to that , the refusal to grant entry visas prevents Members of the European Parliament and of national parliaments from seeing the situation for themselves .
<en> All this is highlighted in my Group 's motion .
<en> However , I think that our criticism of breaches of human rights must be measured by absolute criteria , rather than following a political scale of who in the world plays first fiddle at the moment .
<en> That is not right .
<en> We keep running around in circles ; we have not been able to take a step towards objectivity for millennia .
<en> The Romans were always right and their chroniclers painted it as a wrongdoing when an attacked opponent was bold enough to defend himself .
<en> Let me get back to Belarus , however .
<en> Lukashenko 's regime is first and foremost an attempt to disrespect the direction in which the Euro-Atlantic initiatives are going .
<en> Mr Lukashenko plays in his own narrow field , ignoring the fact that moderate-sized countries cannot behave like that since supranational capital will not allow it .
<en> If you do not obey , you will be isolated and the international community will support the opposition within the country .
<en> That is how it works and we all know it .
<en> Sooner or later Mr Lukashenko and his party machine will pay dearly for acting in this manner .
<en> Belarus is located in an area that is strategically important for the Unites States and for NATO .
<en> The present US Administration and the governments of some other countries would very much like Belarus to join NATO , together with Ukraine and Georgia , thereby causing damage to Russia .
<en> Our worries about human rights in Belarus would not be so intense if , in fact , the real issue was not Russia .
<en> The question is , however , whether attempts to weaken Russia help the issue of world security .
<en> I am rather afraid that such attempts may unleash powers that no one will be able to control .
<en> Russia has been suppressing them for several millennia .
<sp>
<en> author . - ( PL ) Madam President , Commissioner , the Members of the European Parliament who are concerned with the issue of Belarus and who are monitoring the situation in Belarus are faced with contradictory information .
<en> On the one hand there is the desire that has been publicly and officially declared to normalise relations with the European Union .
<en> The opening of the representative office of the European Commission in Minsk is a symbol of this desire .
<en> On the other hand , in the same month , the police brutally attacked demonstrators who wanted to celebrate the nineteenth anniversary of the country 's independence .
<en> The following day the authorities sent KGB special forces to independent journalists .
<en> A month later the activists were handed down long sentences and this is not even the opposition , just people who dared to demonstrate in defence of citizens ' rights and the rights of small businesses , such as Andrei Kim or Sergei Parsukiewicz .
<en> We have also recently heard that Alexander Milinkiewicz was arrested and fined just for meeting Belarus citizens and for discussing public issues with them .
<en> Alexander Kazulin , the most important political prisoner , a prisoner of conscience in contemporary Europe , is still in prison .
<en> Speaking as the chairman of the Belarus delegation I would like to see the day when we can put forward a Resolution to the European Parliament that notes with satisfaction that changes have taken place in Belarus to make that country part of the civilised European Community .
<en> Unfortunately this will not happen today .
<en> Without any guarantees for the fundamental rights of free and democratic elections , to express one 's political opinions , freedom of the press and freedom to practise one 's religion , there is no possibility that the European Union should ever recognise the regime in Belarus as a country with which it is worth cooperating , or as a country that it is worth helping .
<en> We shall never support the policies that are practised by Alexander Lukashenko .
<en> We shall , however , support independent citizens ' groups and individual citizens from Belarus in their contacts with the European Union in the hope that one day the country will return to normality .
<sp>
<en> author . - Madam President , Belarus is a beautiful and important country with much potential for progress which can lead to enviable prosperity for its citizens .
<en> Unfortunately , vital democratic norms are presently much compromised in this country .
<en> This is mainly due to the inability of the governing authorities to come to terms with the need to respect the necessities of freedom of expression and other democratic principles .
<en> Such respect is an indispensable requirement of any non-dictatorial government .
<en> Reports coming out of Belarus of arbitrary arrests of members of civil society and opposition activists , of the use of excessive force against peaceful demonstrators and of repression of independent media journalists are evidence of practices which should , and must , be terminated immediately .
<en> We call on the Belarusian Government to see reason , to change its tactics and to choose the road of freedom and democracy rather than the road of suppression and totalitarianism , which can only lead to worsening of the conflict with its own people and with the international community .

<en> - ( PL ) Mr President , I abstained from voting on Mr Harangoz√≥ 's report .
<en> One of the aims of the European Union 's cohesion policy should be to bolster the instruments of solidarity and integration .
<en> Vulnerable groups and communities should receive our support in the fight against exclusion and inequality .
<en> This should not , however , be seen as a counter-argument to the development of urban areas , as one does not preclude the other .
<en> A territorial approach is important but does not , after all , invalidate the significance of effectiveness in cohesion policy .
<sp>
<en> - ( PL ) Mr President , the Harangoz√≥ report accepted today raises the exceptionally important problem of the impact of cohesion policy on the integration of the most threatened societies and groups .
<en> This report unambiguously stresses the need for a continuation of cohesion policy in areas that are less developed , neglected , where there are difficult farming conditions and where there is weak or outdated infrastructure .
<en> Particular support should be provided for regions and for areas where there is historical developmental retardation , where the local people are less well prepared to meet the difficult challenges of a market economy .
<en> Intra-regional differences in the level of development are very great .
<en> It is therefore necessary to create a factual image of the state of development of our regions and to use this as a basis for getting to grips with difficult areas within individual regions .
<en> We can say right now that this concerns mountainous areas and a significant proportion of rural areas .
<en> We have to put together a sustainable development process so that enclaves of weaker development or backward enclaves are not left behind or created .
<sp>
<en> Mr President , I also abstained on this report .
<en> I would like to make two or three points as to why I did so .
<en> Firstly , I have struggled to believe that the founding fathers of this place , when they were laying the basis for their European Union for freedom and for freedom of movement etc. thought that the detailed policy that is set out in this report would be one of the things that would come forward in years to come .
<en> Secondly , I am not convinced that this should be done at European level - perhaps it could be at national level , but most certainly it should be at the most local of levels .
<en> Finally , I would like to wind up by saying that in my constituency the City of Leicester is an example of how local action in this field can work .
<en> Leicester is one of the most diverse cities in the United Kingdom for all sorts of different reasons - it has both rich and poor , of many different nationalities - and yet , because of individual and local action , Leicester has one of the most coherent strategies for the cohesion and integration , as we say here , of vulnerable communities and groups .
<en> It is an example to us all that local action is best , and I worry when we talk about it at an EU level .
<sp>
<en> Mr President , my comments echo those of the speaker before me .
<en> My comments are also relevant to the Panayotopoulos-Cassiotou report on poverty and social exclusion .
<en> If we take these two reports together they clearly represent a flaw in the thinking of European politicians , namely that whatever the problem appears to be , Europe is the solution .
<en> I urge all of us really concerned with the problems of vulnerable communities to look instead at local-community-led solutions and not the proposals of some distant Eurocrat or some distant Member of the European Parliament .
<en> Please look at the excellent work , for example , of the Centre for Social Justice based in London in my own constituency and led by Iain Duncan-Smith and his wonderful team , who are building an alliance of local community organisations tackling poverty and social exclusion : organisations such as the Croydon Caribbean Credit Union or the London Boxing Academy , attracting some of the most vulnerable people in society .
<en> While the issues in the report are all serious problems , we should remember that the solutions are often to be found closer to home , and for this reason I abstained on the Harangoz√≥ report .
<sp>
<en> ( CS ) Mr President , the sustainable development policy has no chance of succeeding unless it assumes a global dimension .
<en> The UN Millennium Declaration may call on all states to ensure policy coherence for development but developed countries do not take many practical steps in this regard .
<en> Therein lies the contradiction of the undertaking by the European Union , urging us to assess the impact of our European policies concerning the Development Goals .
<en> This makes the fact that we add restrictions to our fisheries policy for the benefit of developing countries even more valuable .
<en> I would also like to mention timber logging in West Africa , where only 5 % of forests are managed sustainably .
<en> Of course it is important for the Commission to financially support the launch of national strategic plans in Africa but we will also be able to prevent the plundering of tropical forests if we prohibit the timber from being imported into Europe unless it has a clear eco-label .
<en> I believe that the Commission will soon table such proposals and that we in this House and the Council will adopt them , without looking for any excuses .

<en> in writing . - President , I spoke on the Morgan report during the debate but I did not have the opportunity to speak on amendment 159 .
<en> This amendment would prohibit Member States from authorising the construction of new power stations that emit more than 350g of carbon dioxide per kilowatt hour produced .
<en> I would like to clarify the position on behalf of the EPLP who have all received a number of letters on this amendment .
<en> Whilst we appreciate that climate change is real and present and we have an obligation to address this , we have voted against amendment 159 because it would knock out the development of all new gas- , oil- and coal-fired power stations .
<en> This would be detrimental to Europe 's security of supply and to keeping the lights on in Europe .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( FR ) I voted against the Morgan report and the energy package because I believe that we are going down the wrong road .
<en> The proposed Agency will be yet another bureaucratic body .
<en> A network of national regulators with extended powers would be a more effective way of ensuring that small producers have access to the networks .
<en> Unbundling has become a kind of magic potion , whereas the experience of those countries that have been practising it certainly does not put the case for liberal measures of this kind .
<en> The energy market is a global market .
<en> Competition for Gazprom and the oil-producing states will come not from the biogas cooperatives but from the big European companies .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( PL ) When it voted for compulsory unbundling of ownership of energy concerns in the European Union , the European Parliament took a decisive step towards creating a common market in electrical energy .
<en> Dividing these concerns into companies responsible for energy production and companies responsible for its transmission is the only way to create an open and competitive market where there is no conflict of interest .
<en> The consumer should be the main beneficiary of the proposed changes .
<en> The proposal adopted significantly strengthens consumers ' rights .
<en> Inter alia , it gives consumers the right to withdraw from a contract with an electricity supplier without additional charges .
<en> Consumers are also given the right to change their energy supplier in a very short time .
<en> It should be borne in mind that the electricity market is currently dominated by monopolies that abuse their position on uncompetitive markets .
<en> I believe that price caps will protect energy users from exploitation by energy concerns , without deterring new entities from entering the market .
<en> Clearly , the solutions proposed will not resolve all the problems related to energy currently confronting us , such as the rise in oil prices .
<en> Nonetheless , these solutions represent appropriate steps towards the development of a more competitive market .
<en> The debate is to continue in the Council .
<en> Unfortunately , however , it is unlikely that all of the European Parliament 's proposals will be accepted .
<en> As the rapporteur rightly pointed out , many Member States protect want to protect their own national interests .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( FR ) This third energy package dogmatically persists in following the course of total separation between the energy production side and the distribution networks .
<en> It is aimed at subjecting the entire energy sector solely to the laws of the free market and to everyone competing with everyone else .
<en> As the same causes produce the same effects this will lead the European Union to an even bigger disaster than that experienced by California in the year 2000 .
<en> This policy is bad for consumers , bad for the industry 's employees , bad for SMEs and SMIs , bad for jobs , bad for security and bad for the environment .
<en> The market and the private sector are incapable of meeting the energy needs of Europeans and of responding to the challenges of global warming and the post fossil fuel era .
<en> Their prime objective is to pay out as much as possible to their shareholders , not to act in the general interests of the nation .
<en> We need a proper internal market for energy in Europe and this will only be achieved on the basis of cooperation .
<en> The energy sector needs to be guided by coordinated public action from the Member States , not by the activities of the financial markets .
<en> The EU has to take steps to ensure that energy is recognised as a global public resource and not as just another commodity to be bought and sold .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - I was disappointed that my own group 's amendment on nuclear accident liability was not adopted .
<en> Nevertheless , the final Morgan report does contain much to commend it , and I welcome the addition of references to the proposed charter on energy consumers ' rights .
<en> On balance , therefore , I was able to vote in favour of the report .

<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( ET ) I strongly support these amendments , as these strengthen free competition in the European Union , help keep prices at reasonable levels and at the same time allow consumers to exercise their freedom to change their electricity supplier any time wished .
<en> Furthermore this boosts cross-border electricity sharing and , with that , also protects states and consumers from sudden electricity shortages .
<en> I call for fast action in this field in eliminating unnecessary bureaucracy and burdens to enable EU electricity companies to act freely throughout the Union to strengthen free competition and to empower consumers to make conscious choices .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( FR ) I voted against this report , which in purporting to lay down common rules for the internal market in electricity is in fact proposing to dismantle the heritage of Europe 's traditional operating networks .
<en> Separating electricity production and electricity distribution will in my view provide no additional guarantees as to the efficiency , security or accessibility of the network , particularly in the present situation of a sustained growth in global electricity demand and major uncertainty over resources .
<en> This latter factor calls for even greater structural investment in order to safeguard our supplies and promote research and innovation , a prospect that seems to be largely incompatible with the philosophy of strong competition and short-term profitability that underlies the decision to move towards the total deregulation of this sector .
<en> The ' third way ' , which is supported by the French Socialists but regrettably was not adopted , appears to be a much more sensible solution since it allows us to preserve the patrimonial integrity of Europe 's large energy groups while at the same time placing the organisation of electricity distribution in the hands of independent regulators .
<en> Nevertheless , I welcome the progress that this report represents as far as consumer protection is concerned , particularly the introduction of rules for combating energy poverty and for ensuring transparency and accessibility to information for the end user .
<sp>
<2en> Supplying electricity is not a trade but a mains service .
<2en> The service must be provided to all stakeholders without interruption and with the lowest possible impact on the environment .
<2en> This requirement is inconsistent with the risks involved in international trade by competing companies .
<2en> Electricity will continue to be a scarce and vulnerable product in the future too , certainly now that fossil fuels are running out and as global warming continues .
<2en> That is why it is good that in many EU Member States it is the State or local authorities that have developed the power stations and electricity grids .
<2en> Privatisation of these mains services is undesirable and risky .
<2en> Their sale creates new owners and a monopoly on the transmission system .
<2en> That system is a non-profit-making resource between production and sale , but ownership of it can be misused to impose a high toll on consumers and any competitors .
<2en> Fixing electricity prices through the stock market leads to consumer prices that are much higher than production costs .
<2en> The EU Member States are right to look at how these risks should be combated .
<2en> The situation varies greatly from one Member State to another .
<2en> It is best that these issues are weighed up there .
<2en> I am in favour of giving the Member States the greatest possible freedom , the third way referred to in the Glante amendment , but I am against this European directive as a whole .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( FR ) Obviously the real aim of this third energy package is not security of supply , the quality of the services being provided , price affordability or the ability of consumers freely to choose their supplier but rather the permanent dismantling of what is left of the old public electricity monopolies .
<en> The determination being displayed by the Commission and by many Members of this House in wanting to impose ' patrimonial separation ' , in other words forcing ' historical ' operators like EDF to give up ownership of their network , is quite unacceptable .
<en> The activities these companies are being accused of , namely restricting competitors ' access to the network and deliberately limiting investment in infrastructure projects , have never in fact been proven .
<en> Neither is it clear how entrusting control of the network to a single operator that is not the electricity supplier can guarantee an appropriate and adequate level of investment , non-abuse of a key position or better congestion management .
<en> This is why , though we have always defended the exclusive primacy of Member States over energy affairs , which is a strategic area of too great importance to be left to the Eurocrats , we will be supporting as the lesser of two evils the ' effective separation ' solution being proposed by , among others , France and Germany .
<en> We shall also vote against those texts whose viewpoints we fundamentally reject .
<sp>
<en> in writing . - ( PT ) I could only vote in favour of this report .
<en> To say yes to all the forces for liberalisation of the electricity market is to say yes to a fairer , more competitive and more transparent market .
<en> However , it is not only the correctness of this report , which places the consumer at the heart of the issue , that attracts me .
<en> With increasing energy prices and a lack of competition in national markets , there is a danger of increasing the number of citizens excluded from accessing energy .
<en> I therefore agree with the social concerns expressed as , for the first time , the concept of ' fuel poverty ' has been defined , drawing attention to the importance of the Member States developing national plans which cover all citizens .
<en> Given the current situation in the national energy markets within the EU , it is unacceptable for one company to both own the electricity network and also be responsible for the transmission of electricity , thus holding a de facto monopoly , as it can then block access to the market for new operators who , in many cases , are more competitive .
<en> This document therefore courageously identifies the need to increase the level of transparency and competition within the energy sector , while effectively protecting the consumer from the consequences of a closed and inflexible market .

<en> in writing . - The fishing industry has faced many crises over the years , but none greater than at present , with rising fuel prices which are pushing the industry over the edge to the point where it can no longer survive .
<en> The continuing spiralling price of oil could prove to be disastrous for many industries , but none is more vulnerable than the fishing industry , with jobs at sea and on shore at risk .
<en> We must look into all the options which are available to us .
<en> One route that should be explored is reducing taxes in order to ensure that fuel costs come down .
<en> May I ask the following question : if we do not have fishermen , where will the fish we require come from ?
<en> Are we going to sit back and allow foreign imports to take over our markets and put our industry out of business ?

<en> However , I am confident that with good will and all-round cooperation it is possible .
<en> I welcome yesterday 's statement from the Commission announcing its intention to provide emergency assistance to fishing fleets .
<en> I sincerely hope that these measures will be formally adopted by the Council of Fisheries Ministers next week and then swiftly implemented .

<en> in writing . - ( FR ) The dramatic rise in the price of diesel oil , 300 % since 2003 has made its full impact felt in the fisheries sector .
<en> With the continuously worsening crisis , many fishing undertakings are now in a very fragile financial state .
<en> Fisheries are in fact a particularly important pillar in the economic and social development of the outermost regions .
<en> Moreover , they are hit all the harder by the rise in the price of fuel because of their remote geographical location .
<en> That is an unacceptable situation .
<en> The European Union has a duty to find a compromise .
<en> The European Parliament has just sent out a strong signal to fishers .
<en> In calling for the official aid ceiling to be raised to EUR 100 000 per vessel and not per undertaking , in calling for the immediate application of emergency and social support measures and , lastly , in demanding the reorganisation of European Fund expenditure for fisheries , MEPs have made it clear to fishers that they have heard their distress call .
<en> The Council of European fisheries ministers will be discussing these proposals on 23 and 24 June 2008 .
<en> The European Union has no option but to restore the confidence of fishers in order to plug the huge hole that has recently appeared .

<en> in writing . - ( PT ) It is well-known that Russia is an important strategic partner for the European Union , and our geography makes us dependent on each other .
<en> Diplomacy must therefore be used to find the best solutions for this unavoidable proximity .
<en> The need to cooperate , however , must not force us into a real or disguised blindness towards the serious problems Russia raises .

<en> Mr President , this debate is about the nuts and bolts of Parliament , and it is our duty to ask if the proposals about groups are practical .
<en> It was certainly with practicalities in mind , faced with the basic requirement of 30 Members , that I submitted my amendment - I think it was my amendment , Mr Corbett - which enabled the President of Parliament , with the agreement of the Conference of Presidents , to allow a group to continue its work for a limited period if it fell below that particular threshold .
<en> In committee it was generally agreed this was a good idea to avoid a group being held hostage by a Member threatening to leave and thereby instantly disbanding such a group .
<en> That is why I am somewhat attracted by this new compromise which has been proposed for a limit of 25 Members .
<en> It does seem to me to be a sensible idea , which would alleviate one of the difficulties I was referring to when I prepared my amendment .
<en> We must always remember , however , that we were elected to represent the views and interests of our electorate as a whole .
<en> It is a fact that our European electoral spectrum spans an ever-wider variety of opinion , which is good for democracy .
<en> It is not just the number of Members which increases in this Parliament ; it is also the diversity of views which they bring with them .
<en> If we are successfully to fulfil our parliamentary mandate , we must have the opportunity to fully mirror the views of our national electorates .
<en> A small group in the European Parliament here may well represent a large body of opinion in Member States .
<en> We need to be able to work constructively as a Parliament and also , most importantly , in line with the wishes of the people that we represent , however that is formulated in the disposition and composition of our groups .
<en> So , whilst I welcome this possible compromise , I welcome a sensible and pragmatic approach to this matter .
<en> I hope that we do not allow ourselves to fall into the trap of assuming that fewer groups necessarily means more democracy .

<en> ( BG ) Mr. President , colleagues , I think that the motion in the report of Mr. Corbett deserves attention and , in my opinion , comes just on time , since actually with its adoption we do not threaten any of the currently existing groups in the European Parliament .
<en> I am in support of a more effectively functioning Parliament in the next mandate from 2009 to 2014 .
<en> We have discussed the meaning of these changes repeatedly and limitation of the opportunities of Members elected to the European parliament to express their opinion has never been discussed .
<en> But since our Parliament is a large Parliament , maybe , as we say the largest democratically elected parliament in the world , its essence of European Parliament is held precisely by the parliamentary groups , by the political groups that represent not the nations of the elected Members who participate in them , but represent the political trends which unite the Members .
<en> This is also the meaning of the great power , opportunities which both the political groups and their leaders have in the activity of our Parliament .
<en> That is why I think that now , too , should we blunder in the direction of blaming Socialists or Christian Democrats of being undemocratic , we will not be right .
<en> Quite the contrary , I think that in this way we shall provide the opportunity for a much clearer profile of the political groups which manage to form and actually operate in the next mandate of the European Parliament .
<en> Of course , I also think that it is easy to speak in the name of a political group which is not threatened with failure to come up with the necessary number of Members in the next parliament .
<en> I think that in any case the groups that exist today will be able to continue to exist over the next mandate .
<en> In addition , our presence here , in this Parliament , is largely due to the power of the political parties we represent .
<en> We should not consider the one in isolation from the other .
<en> That is why we should not think , either , that the political life of Europe unconditionally revolves here , in Parliament , and depends on the two political groups , nor should we forget the parties we represent .
<en> And in this sense I suggest that we really move toward the suggested compromise and support the motion of Mr. Corbett .
<sp>
<en> Mr President , this Parliament frequently talks about openness , transparency and democracy , but does not always display it .
<en> In this instance , the rapporteur , Mr Corbett , has been very open and transparent about what he seeks to achieve : he wants to make it harder for small groups to form and function ; he wants to deny them the resources and privileges they are currently entitled to , which enables them to represent the will of those who elected them .
<en> Mr Corbett wants to put political groups that he does not approve of out of business if he possibly can .
<en> This is totally undemocratic .
<en> Why should not the will of European electors be expressed in political groups , formed by those they elect , however small those groups may be .

<en> ( PT ) Mr President , Parliament needs to interpret Democracy in a democratic fashion .
<en> This means that the Rules of Procedure should not be taken in isolation ; rather they must be interpreted in the light of the moral basis for suffrage and the principle of representation as signifying self-legislation and citizens ' autonomy .
<en> Drawing some points from this principle , I should like to say the following : from my point of view , the amendment Mr Corbett has proposed is correct in principle , but the reason why a group that falls below the minimum threshold necessary during a parliamentary term must continue to exist lies especially in the fact that voters ' democratic choices are also nearly always made taking account of the EP political group that candidates belong to .
<en> Voters are not indifferent to whether a candidate is elected to sit on the benches of the Socialist Group in the European Parliament or of the Group of the European People 's Party ( Christian Democrats ) and European Democrats .
<en> This being the case , I believe that this amendment , rather than containing a discretionary power for the President of Parliament , should contain a binding power , rather than a permission , a duty , and the period for continuation of the group can only , from a democratic point of view , be exactly the period of a parliamentary term .
<en> Otherwise we would be completely subverting the principles of freedom that make up what we are .
<en> My second remark concerns the temptation to copy what the national parliaments do .
<en> National parliaments really do act as models for us , but in this case we need to copy them cum grano salis , with caution , as the proliferation of groups in European democracy can make up for the lack of representativity that hurls Europe from one crisis to another .
<en> Proliferation here may make up for the persistent divorce between European citizens and those who represent them .
<en> Additionally , the more plurality there is , the more evident the struggle and intense politicking that normally lead to our consensuses will become , as systematic consensuses are not free from controversy here either .
<en> Having many groups can help Parliament politicise bureaucratic Europe , because a Democracy is a Democracy and not an Order .

<en> If China wishes to play a bigger role on the world stage , it must shoulder the resultant responsibilities .

<en> I noted the comparison with the USSR of Brezhnev .

<en> We played a key role in achieving this progress , and it is also through dialogue and through democratic developments that our values prevailed , as always .
<en> We must have a challenging dialogue with China where no subject is taboo , and we must encourage it to make commitments in all areas , in the political , human rights and social fields .
<en> Indeed , some Members have mentioned the death penalty .
<en> We should also address this issue with China , but we must also address it with all the other countries , and I hope that the same conservative Members who have spoken just now on the subject will do so .
<en> I should like to remind you that there are other countries where the death penalty is in force that have relations with the European Union ; however , we do need to have this comprehensive dialogue .
<en> We must also proceed with caution , and I am in full agreement with what the Commission said with regard to the Council , that we should not exacerbate nationalist feelings in China at a time when it is playing host to a very important event for the whole country , a country which is seeking to achieve its integration into the international arena .
